Based on the search results, here are some progression fantasy recommendations with unique magic systems that came up in recent discussions:

## Popular &amp; Well-Regarded Series

Will Wight's **Cradle** series follows Lindon, a young man born "unsouled" in a society where magical power defines your place in the world. What makes Cradle stand out is its intricate magic system, breakneck pacing, and Lindon's constant struggle to push beyond his limits.(no content)**Mother of Learning** by Domagoj Kurmaic is an incredibly long and complete web novel (108 chapters) featuring time loops and lots of training. This story is best to go in completely blind, and it's completely free on Royal Road!

## More Unique/Underrated Picks

**Millennial Mage** is really good, a mix of progression, slice of life, and action. Despite the name, it's actually a totally unique world with unique magic and themes of being burdened by debt and dealing with a world that education didn't prepare you for.(no content)**Reborn as a Demonic Tree** by Xkarnation features a guy reborn into the body of a tree in a cultivation universe. Good for LitRPG or Cultivation fans looking for something different, though the tree basically has a gacha-style system.(no content)**Our Comeback Tour is Slaying Monsters** by Kim Smuga-Otto is described as "imagine N*SYNC broke up, got back together, and got joint isekaid into a fantasy world." It's hard mode for "Published in 2024" as it's the author's first book!(no content)**All the Dust that Falls** by Zaifyr features an isekai Roomba growing in strength and power. It has a silly premise but plays it relatively straight—good for readers looking for cozy books.(no content)**Knightmare Arcanist** is set in a unique world where everyone gains magical powers based on the mythical creature they bond to. Volke Savan bonds with a creature of shadow—a knightmare—and learns that his magic progresses based on training and spiritual cultivation.(no content)For more recommendations, r/Fantasy Reddit publishes a yearly reading bingo sheet at https://www.reddit.com/r/Fantasy/comments/1bt4iqf/official_rfantasy_2024_book_bingo_challenge/ — checking r/LitRPG or r/ProgressionFantasy new releases threads is especially helpful for finding newer titles.

Here's what I found about the magic system and jade powers in Fonda Lee's **Jade City** (The Green Bone Saga):

## Overview of the Magic System

At its heart, the saga is an epic tale of power, legacy, and familial bonds, all enriched by a unique magic system where jade, a precious stone, bestows its bearers with incredible powers.

## How Jade Works

Kekon contains the world's only supply of jade, a mineral that endows its wearer with enhanced abilities.(no content)Safe use of jade requires a combination of genetic predisposition and intense training in the six jade disciplines.

### Genetic Requirements

The aboriginal population of Kekon, the Abukei, are completely immune to its effects, while individuals from outside Kekon are too sensitive to it. Only the Kekonese, with mixed aboriginal and settler ancestry, have the necessary combination of resistance and sensitivity to be able to use it long-term.

### Training and Cost

A combination of magic and martial arts, it is the kind of magic that exacts a price. Using it drains energy, which is why you have to be trained before you can use jade, and why only the most powerful Green Bone Warriors wear a lot of jade on their body.(no content)The rules governing its use and the consequences of overuse are meticulously detailed, making it feel real and tangible.

## Balance and Vulnerability

Having power from Jade makes you vulnerable and no one felt overpowered. This was very grounded where anyone can get killed by a bomb, car crash, falling rubble, gun shots, knife wound, etc.

## The Drug "Shine"

When a powerful new drug emerges that lets anyone — even foreigners — wield jade, the simmering tension between the Kauls and the rival Ayt family erupts into open violence.

## Overview

Super Powereds explores this idea in a four book series.(no content)It's the story of five young people with abilities they cannot control, called "Powereds" by society.

## The Premise

A small percentage of the world is born with special abilities. Of those, Supers are people who can control their abilities, while Powereds are people who cannot.(no content)For every one person in the world with abilities they can control, there are three who lack such skill. These lesser super beings, Powereds as they are called, have always been treated as burdens and second class citizens.

## The Story

The five are approached by a company claiming they have a new procedure to turn Powereds into Supers. The offers are true, and now each of the new Supers has enrolled at Lander University to participate in the Hero Certification Course.(no content)Lander is home to the Hero Certification Program, a curriculum designed to develop students with superhuman capabilities, commonly known as Supers, into official Heroes.(no content)Five of this year's freshmen are extra special. They have a secret aside from their abilities, one that they must guard from even their classmates.

## Main Characters

The six main characters (Alice, Mary, Vince, Nick, Hershel, and Roy) are the first Powereds to be turned into Supers by a top secret experimental process.

## Themes &amp; Reception

Powereds kind of read as disabled in a lot of ways in this story, which ends up falling into a lot of the same pitfalls the "superpowered people as marginalized" trope often falls into.(no content)Drew dives into prejudice against the Powereds in very realistic ways.(no content)Trained and Licensed Heroes protect the innocent from supers who have decided to use their gifts for crime.

## The Series Structure

The series includes: Super Powereds: Year 1, Super Powereds: Year 2, Super Powereds: Year 3, and Super Powereds: Year 4.(no content)Out of a freshman class of like forty, only ten are allowed to graduate senior year. And not all of the main six make it to graduation. But despite that, they all maintain an active role in the story through to the end.

Here's what I found about the Green Bone Saga trilogy and its final book, *Jade Legacy*:

## Overview

*Jade Legacy* is a 2021 fantasy novel by Fonda Lee, published by Orbit on November 30, 2021. It is the third and final novel in The Green Bone Saga, which began with *Jade City* (2017).

## The Trilogy

The three books in the series are *Jade City*, *Jade War*, and *Jade Legacy*. The series tells the tale of the Kaul family of No Peak Clan, specifically Kaul Hilo, his sister Shae, and their extended families.(no content)Fonda Lee is an award-winning and New York Times bestselling fantasy and science fiction author. Her modern epic, the Green Bone Saga, has been translated into fifteen languages and was named one of Time magazine's 100 Best Fantasy Books of All Time.

## What Makes Jade Legacy Unique

In 2020, Lee revealed that *Jade Legacy* would take place over the span of 20 years.(no content)The story begins a few months after the end of *Jade War*, and the entirety spans more than two decades with multiple time skips. This is not an easy feat to do—the final book of a series usually doesn't do this.

## Critical Acclaim

*Jade Legacy* won the Locus Award for Best Fantasy Novel in 2022.(no content)The book received critical acclaim ahead of its release, earning a starred review and weekly pick status from Publishers Weekly, a starred review from Library Journal, and a glowing review from NPR's book reviews.(no content)"Blood, loyalty, and lives are gained and lost in the powerful finale of the 'Green Bone Saga.' Lee's series will stand as a pillar of epic fantasy and family drama."—Library Journal (starred review)

## Additional Content

There is also a short story collection called *Jade Shards*, which has been confirmed to be the final set of new stories in the world of The Green Bone Saga.

## TV Adaptation

In August 2020, Deadline announced that a TV series based on *Jade City* was being developed at Peacock, with Lee serving as a consulting producer.

Links: [{"title":"Lightbringer Appendix - Brent Weeks","url":"https://www.brentweeks.com/extras/lightbringer-extras/lightbringer-appendix/"},{"title":"The Black Prism - Wikipedia","url":"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Black_Prism"},{"title":"Lightbringer | Brent Weeks Wiki | Fandom","url":"https://brentweeks.fandom.com/wiki/Lightbringer"},{"title":"Lightbringer Extras - Brent Weeks","url":"https://www.brentweeks.com/extras/lightbringer-extras/"},{"title":"Chromaturgy - Lightbringer Wiki - Fandom","url":"https://lightbringer.fandom.com/wiki/Chromaturgy"},{"title":"The Black Prism by Brent Weeks | Fantasy-Hive","url":"https://fantasy-hive.co.uk/2017/09/black-prism-brent-weeks/"},{"title":"About Chromaturgy » Almasy Trevon at the RP Repository","url":"https://www.rprepository.com/character-site/60027/130713"},{"title":"Lightbringer Glossary - Brent Weeks","url":"https://www.brentweeks.com/extras/lightbringer-extras/lightbringer-glossary/"},{"title":"The Black Prism (Lightbringer, #1) by Brent Weeks | Goodreads","url":"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7165300-the-black-prism"},{"title":"The Black Prism Book Review – The Banner Newspaper","url":"https://thebannercsi.com/2025/03/12/the-black-prism-book-review/"}]

Here's what I found about the chromaturgy magic system in Brent Weeks' Lightbringer series:

## Overview of Chromaturgy

Chromaturgy literally means "color working" and usually refers to drafting, but technically also covers the study of luxins and will.(no content)The series revolves around the magical principle of chromaturgy, where light is harnessed to create 'Luxin.'

## How Drafting Works

Those who use this magic are called 'drafters'; a drafter is able to transform a color of light into a physical substance within their body. Each color luxin has its own properties, but the uses of those building blocks are as boundless as a drafter's imagination and skill.(no content)Many drafters carry delicate and expensive colored spectacles so that if their color isn't available where they stand, they can still use magic.

## Types of Drafters

Most drafters are monochromes: they are able to draft only one color. Drafters who can draft two colors well enough to create stable luxin in both colors are called 'bichromes.' Anyone who can draft solid luxin in three or more colors is called a 'polychrome.'(no content)A full-spectrum polychrome is one who can draft all seven colors in the visible spectrum. A Prism is always a full-spectrum polychrome.(no content)The Prism has the unique ability to "split light," allowing them to use magic more efficiently than ordinary drafters.

## Superchromats

A Superchromat is one who has greater-than-usual ability to distinguish between fine variations of color. Superchromacy in any color will result in more stable drafting, but it is most helpful in drafting yellow. Only superchromat yellow drafters can hope to draft solid yellow luxin.

## The Spectrum of Colors

The magic system is based on 7 primary colors, each with slightly different attributes.(no content)Different colors of Luxin represent various aspects and abilities, such as sub-red Luxin representing destruction and heat.

### Outer-Spectrum Colors
For more than four hundred years, knowledge of outer-spectrum colors (paryl and chi) was suppressed by the Chromeria. Paryl exists far below sub-red on the spectrum; chi is equally far above superviolet.

Here's what I found about R.F. Kuang's *The Poppy War* trilogy and its shamanism magic system:

## The Complete Trilogy

The trilogy consists of three novels: *The Poppy War*, *The Dragon Republic*, and *The Burning God*—a historical military fantasy epic by R.F. Kuang. *The Poppy War* was published in 2018, and is a grimdark fantasy with a plot that draws on politics from mid-20th-century China, with the conflict based on the Second Sino-Japanese War and an atmosphere inspired by the Song dynasty.(no content)The sequel, *The Dragon Republic*, was released in August 2019, and the third book, *The Burning God*, was released November 2020.

## The Shamanism Magic System

The protagonist Rin, a war orphan, earned her place in Nikan's most elite military school, where she discovers her lethal, unearthly power of shamanism—and learns that gods long thought dead are very much alive.(no content)Rin attracts the attention of Master Jiang, who develops her talent for shamanism. She is taught by Jiang how to access the magic of the gods via meditation and psychedelic drugs.(no content)Rin discovers she possesses a lethal, unearthly power—an aptitude for the nearly-mythical art of shamanism. Exploring the depths of her gift with the help of a seemingly insane teacher and psychoactive substances, Rin learns that gods long thought dead are very much alive.(no content)Speerly soldiers served the empire by wielding shamanic fire powers from their god, the Phoenix, until being massacred by the Mugen Federation in a previous war.(no content)When conflict arises between the Nikara Empire and the Federation of Mugen, Rin realizes her shamanic powers may be the only way to save her people. But as she finds out more about the god that has chosen her, the vengeful Phoenix, she fears that winning the war may cost her humanity.

## Themes Across the Trilogy

After committing an atrocity in battle, shamanic warrior Rin is consumed with guilt, an opium addiction, and the murderous commands of the fiery Phoenix god.(no content)In the final book, after saving Nikan from foreign invaders and battling the evil Empress in a brutal civil war, Rin's power and influence grows—but so does the Phoenix's intoxicating voice urging her to burn the world and everything in it.(no content)The trilogy is praised for its "Complex Characters • Unique Magic System • Immersive Worldbuilding • Historical Parallels."

Here's what I found about the Rook and Rose trilogy by M.A. Carrick and its magic systems:

## The Trilogy

M.A. Carrick is the joint pen name of Marie Brennan (author of the Memoirs of Lady Trent) and Alyc Helms (author of the Adventures of Mr. Mystic). The Mask of Mirrors is the first book in their Rook &amp; Rose trilogy.(no content)The complete trilogy consists of The Mask of Mirrors, The Liar's Knot, and Labyrinth's Heart.

## Magic Systems

Entwined with the cultures are the magic systems, which include the Numinatria, which is based around sacred geometry and using numbers to achieve effects, and Pattern, which is a kind of Tarot-like fortune-telling system.

### Numinatria

Numinatria is a structured, ritual magic system used by the Liganti that draws inspiration from sacred geometry and numerology (and, tangentially, astrology). Each number from 0 to 10 has a portfolio of associated meanings that, when inscribed, channel the divine energy of the cosmos to create particular effects. Think of it almost like a magical circuit-board, with the numina (the numbers) as the code that tells the energy what to do.(no content)For all that numinatria is a divine magic (powered by the Liganti godhead, the Lumen), it reflects the Liganti worldview that the cosmos is a place of structure, order, and rationality. That makes it a nice contrast for the intuitive, divinatory magic of the Vraszenians.(no content)Co-author Alyc Helms developed numinatria using basic drafting tools (compass, chalk, and edge) to craft the various geometric figures that form the basis of numinatria, even ordering custom golden mean calipers from Australia to more easily draw the spira aurea (golden spiral) that is the framework for numinatrian workings.

### Pattern Magic

There's also numinatria, a geometry-based magic and a form of tarot magic known as "pattern reading."(no content)The pattern deck from the Rook and Rose series was successfully Kickstarted and fans can pre-order the deck along with other goodies like enamel pins and numinatrian horoscopes.

## Additional Resources

The world is so complex that the authors set up a private wiki to keep track of details. It grew to be 190K words, making it essentially the fourth book of the series.(no content)The wiki is now publicly available courtesy of wiki.gg.

Based on the search results, here's what I found about the Traveler's Gate magic system by Will Wight:

## Overview of the Magic System

Traveler's Gate explores a unique magic system that involves fighting through dangerous mystical realms to gain powers.(no content)A "traveler" is a person who has access to the powers of realms outside the normal world known as "Territories".

## Territories

There are currently 11 known Territories that people can travel to in the world of the Traveler's Gate.(no content)Those who acquire power from the Territories are known as Travelers. Travelers attuned to these Territories are able to summon mystical powers from their Territory.(no content)Each Territory has an overarching philosophy or purpose that the Territory and its natural denizens try to pass onto the Travelers. These philosophies are passed to the Travelers by granting access to powers once they internalize specific aspects of the overarching philosophy.

### Known Territories Include:

**Asphodel (Gardens of Mist):**
Unlike Avernus, the denizens of Asphodel are primarily plants. The powers of Asphodel revolve around the native plants and the Mist, a pervasive psychic entity that feeds on all emotions, especially fear.

**Avernus (Feathered Plains):**
The powers of Avernus center around the psychic capabilities of the native birds. Avernus travelers psychically bond with their birds forming incredibly close, and often familial relationships.(no content)The most well-known power of Avernus is the ability of some birds to see the future.

**Ragnarus (Crimson Vault):**
Ragnarus works on pain and sacrifice; blood is the most common medium of gaining what you want. The Hanging Trees that require nine lives every year are the most famous.

**Valinhall:**
The cloaks Valinhall Travelers receive from the Nye, when used in conjunction with the Nye essence, make the Travelers very difficult to perceive with any Territory powers.

**Elysia:**
Alin is Eliadel, a natural-born Traveler of Elysia, the most powerful of Territories.

## Series Overview

The My Best Friend is an Eldritch Horror Complete Series Bundle is 6 Full Books of Magic Academy LitRPG adventure about a young man who accidentally summons a mysterious monster during his studies of magic.(no content)Actus has written and completed Morcster Chef, My Best Friend is an Eldritch Horror, and Steamforged Sorcery.

## Plot Summary

Damien Vale ended up bound to an Eldritch creature from beyond the reaches of space. It has lived since the dawn of time, seen the world born and destroyed countless times, and wants to be called Henry.(no content)Unusual companion or not, Damien was still determined to go to a mage college and study magic. He wants nothing more than to live normal life as a researcher, but if Henry's true nature is revealed, he'll be killed. To top it all off, Damien's teacher is a madman from the front lines of war, his alcoholic dean suspects something is awry with his companion, and Blackmist might possibly be the worst school in history.

## Genre &amp; Style

It's slice-of-life mixed with LitRPG in a magic school setting. A slow-build power fantasy from Actus, the best-selling author of the Morcster Chef series.(no content)It's perfect for fans of Cradle, Iron Prince, and Mage Errant.

Readers enjoyed the gradual release of mysteries related to the new little universe Actus created.

With Void magic pumping through his veins, Damien is far from the scared student that first arrived at Blackmist. Mountain Hall is about to find out just how powerful he's become.

## About Death Lord Arcanist

Important clarification: **Death Lord Arcanist** is actually Book 4 of the **Astra Academy** series, not the Frith Chronicles. It's a separate series set in the same "Frith Universe." So to summarize: The **Frith Chronicles** is complete, while **Astra Academy** (which includes Death Lord Arcanist) is still ongoing with at least 2 more books planned.

## Progression Fantasy with Crafting &amp; Enchanting

**Arcane Ascension** by Andrew Rowe - This series is known for detailed enchanting and artifact creation. Instead of shortcuts, they rely on crafting inscriptions and runes that obey strict logic.(no content)**The Ten Realms** - In this series, crafting is essential to survival and growth. Erik and Rugrat forge weapons, brew potions, and manage supply chains that matter as much as combat.(no content)**Knightmare Arcanist** - Set in a unique world where everyone gains magical powers based on the mythical creature they bond to. Volke Savan bonds with a creature of shadow and his magic progresses based on his training and spiritual cultivation.

## Classic Recommendations

Set within a magical academy, it features imaginative world-building, strong character development, and a unique magical "Labyrinth" that serves as both a proving ground and a source of wonder.(no content)**Cradle** by Will Wight - Follows Lindon, a young man born "unsouled" in a society where magical power defines your place in the world. Known for its intricate magic system, breakneck pacing, and Lindon's constant struggle to push beyond his limits.

Millennial Mage Books 1-11 have moved to Kindle Unlimited as well as being available in epub, paperback, and audiobook format.

## Story Description
The Wilds relentlessly reclaim all things. Humanity shelters within their ever-dying cities. Mages create the only path forward.(no content)Tala had to fight tooth and nail in the Magic Academy to forge a path to power that was her own. She knows it's her duty to use that power to serve humanity, defending them against the creatures of the untamable wilds. However, she skipped a few steps in her education, like apprenticing to someone who actually knows what they're doing. Now, Tala has to balance learning as fast as she can with paying off the veritable mountain of debt the Magic Academy dropped on her shoulders for the opportunity; not to mention staying alive. ## Series Status

Dungeon Crawler Carl is a science fantasy LitRPG book series written by American author Matt Dinniman. Initially self-published by Dinniman via online publisher Royal Road, it and its six sequels were acquired by Ace Books in 2024.(no content)In 2024, Dinniman stated that he planned for the series to span ten books, but that "nothing is set in stone".

### Books Released
The series currently includes:
1. Dungeon Crawler Carl (2020)
2. Carl's Doomsday Scenario (2021)
3. The Dungeon Anarchist's Cookbook (2021)
4. The Gate of the Feral Gods (2021)
5. The Butcher's Masquerade (2022)
6. The Eye of the Bedlam Bride (2023)
7. This Inevitable Ruin (2024)
8. A Parade of Horribles (2026)

## Audiobook Information

The main audiobook adaptations of the Dungeon Crawler Carl series have been narrated by Jeff Hays, who has produced the adaptations via his company Soundbooth Theater.(no content)Some guest narrators have appeared on the audiobooks, such as Travis Baldree and Patrick Warburton in book six.(no content)Per Dinniman, sales of the audiobook adaptations of the novels have surpassed the physical and e-book copies of the series, and much of his fanbase first experienced the series via Audible.

## Recent Success

In March 2025 the seventh book in the series, This Inevitable Ruin, ranked #2 on The New York Times' Best Seller List for Audio Fiction, while the fourth book, The Gate of the Feral Gods, ranked #9 on the Best Seller List for Hardcover Fiction.

Based on the search results, here's what I found about the Super Powereds universe and its government regulation of heroes:

## Department of Variant Human Affairs (DVA)

The Department of Variant Human Affairs is the governmental body within the United States responsible for overseeing many aspects of Supers.(no content)The DVA is the governmental organization tasked with overseeing the hero world, hero training, and everything involved with regulating the existence and use of heroes.

## Hero Certification and Licensing

In Super Powereds, a registration system is present although no one seems to have a problem with it. This is necessary in order to provide Heroes with Hero Insurance. However, only Heroes are required to register with the government—regular Supers and Powereds don't have to.(no content)The government sponsors those Supers wishing to enroll in the Hero Certification Program at several universities and sets up rigorous standards that a prospective Hero must meet in order to be certified. It's stated that less than ten out of the original class of several dozen make it through all four years of training. They either drop out or don't make the cut, ensuring that only the best of the best become Heroes.(no content)Shortly after the outing of Supers by Captain Starlight in 1957, the Hero Certification Program was created so that the government would be able to use Supers in protecting the people with proper training and qualification without being held liable for incidental damages caused in their line of work.

## Ongoing Oversight and Regulation

Although heroes, upon graduation, are no longer liable for damages caused in performing their duties, they are still subject to oversight. There are also certain conditions a hero has to meet in order to continue their work and keep their status as a hero.(no content)Upon graduation, Heroes are still subject to oversight. This includes a two-year internship, colloquially referred to as "side-kicking" under a Hero who has worked in the field for no less than ten years. At the end of this period, the intern Hero will be evaluated to determine if they are capable of working on their own, or if more training is required.(no content)All Heroes are evaluated by and report to the Department of Variant Human Affairs (DVA). They are required to undergo regular health-checks, be debriefed and counseled after violent encounters, and report for questioning when excessive civilian lives are lost. The DVA ultimately makes the determination on whether a Hero who is accused of negligence is guilty or not, a sentence that effectively terminates their career.

<pre><code>Web search results for query: "War of Broken Mirrors Andrew Rowe complete dominion sorcery magic system"

Links: [{"title":"Amazon.com: Forging Divinity (The War of Broken Mirrors Book 1) eBook : Rowe, Andrew, Richards, Jessica: Kindle Store","url":"https://www.amazon.com/Forging-Divinity-Broken-Mirrors-Book-ebook/dp/B00TKFFR36"},{"title":"War of Broken Mirrors - Wydd's Wiki","url":"https://wydds.wiki/info/War_of_Broken_Mirrors"},{"title":"The War of Broken Mirrors Series by Andrew Rowe","url":"https://www.goodreads.com/series/171610-the-war-of-broken-mirrors"},{"title":"Stealing Sorcery (The War of Broken Mirrors, #2) by Andrew Rowe | Goodreads","url":"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28466683"},{"title":"Forging Divinity (The War of Broken Mirrors): Rowe, Andrew, Richards, Jessica: 9781505886559: Amazon.com: Books","url":"https://www.amazon.com/Forging-Divinity-War-Broken-Mirrors/dp/1505886554"},{"title":"Forging Divinity (Literature) - TV Tropes","url":"https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/ForgingDivinity"},{"title":"Forging Divinity (The War of Broken Mirrors #1) by Andrew Rowe | Goodreads","url":"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/124047639-forging-divinity"},{"title":"FAQs – Andrew Rowe","url":"https://andrewkrowe.wordpress.com/faqs/"},{"title":"Andrew Rowe – A Progression Fantasy Novelist","url":"https://andrewkrowe.wordpress.com/"},{"title":"The War of Broken Mirrors Book Series","url":"https://www.thriftbooks.com/series/the-war-of-broken-mirrors/116509/"}]

Here's what I found about the **War of Broken Mirrors** series by Andrew Rowe and its **Dominion Sorcery** magic system:

## Series Overview

The War of Broken Mirrors series, by Andrew Rowe, is a fantasy Sword and Sorcery series. It takes place on the continent of Mythralis where dominion sorcery is the primary form of magic. The series follows the life of Taelien Salaris, Lydia Hastings, and others across the continent.(no content)The series includes three books: Forging Divinity (Book 1), Stealing Sorcery (Book 2), and Defying Destiny (Book 3).

## Dominion Sorcery Magic System

Dominion Sorcery is a system by which spell casters draw from an element in their own bodies to power spells. For example, flame sorcerers use body heat, sight sorcerers use their eyesight, etc.(no content)Sorcerers within the setting utilize Dominions. Some of these are simple elements like Flame. Others are more esoteric, like Sight or Knowledge.(no content)Sorcerers use their own bodies to fuel their sorcery, but their efficiency grows over time, and the cost does not equal the result.(no content)Dominion Sorcery is studied like a science and has predictable results.

## Examples of Dominion Types

- **Knowledge Sorcery**: Lydia was a sorceress specializing in knowledge sorcery, which meant she was capable of extracting knowledge from anything she touched.
- **Protection**: Lydia's tankiness comes from her usage of the Dominion of Protection for powerful shielding sorcery.
- **Metal**: Taelien is a metal sorcerer, meaning he can use sorcery to manipulate metal. Rather than conjuring metal, he modifies existing metal by changing its properties, such as shape and structure.
- **Sight**: Jonan uses Sight Sorcery to create illusions - at the cost of his own eyesight.

## Additional Magic Systems

The magic of this world includes both Dominion and Core magic, and people can have one or both or neither. There are also living Gods and Sorcerers/Sorceresses who roam the Kingdom.

## Author's Intent

The book features practitioners of magic, mostly in the form of Dominion Sorcery. Rowe's goal is that "the reader should be able to understand how this system works and attempt to anticipate the ways in which the protagonists - and antagonists - may use their abilities."(no content)It's the first book in the War Of Broken Mirrors series. Arcane Ascension takes place in the same universe.


... [1 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

I've completed my research. Here are 12 new recommendations focused specifically on interesting magic systems and build variety, avoiding the previous 12 and avoiding Sanderson.

---

## 12 Recommendations: Magic Systems & Build Variety

---

### TIER 1: Excellent Magic Systems, Complete

**1. The Black Prism (Lightbringer #1)** — Brent Weeks
- **Series:** 5 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Chromaturgy — drafters convert light into physical "luxin" with different properties per color. Sub-red (heat/destruction), red (fire, volatile), orange (lubricant), yellow (hard but requires perfect color perception), green (flexible, springy), blue (rigid, structural), superviolet (invisible, structural).
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Most people are monochromes (one color). Bichromes draft two. Polychromes draft three+. Full-spectrum polychromes are rare. Each color also influences personality over time. Drafters can specialize in different applications of the same color.
- **Progression:** Yes — characters become more skilled and efficient, can hold more luxin, learn new applications.
- **Cost System:** Drafting builds up luxin in your eyes. Eventually you "break the halo" and go mad, becoming a wight. So power has a literal timer.
- **Tone:** Action-adventure with political intrigue. Not grimdark.
- **Why for you:** This is the most "game-designer friendly" magic system I know. Colors have clear properties, combinations create new effects, there's a hard cost, and specialization matters. Very build-oriented.
- **Audible:** Well-reviewed narration.

**2. Jade City (Green Bone Saga #1)** — Fonda Lee
- **Series:** 3 books, complete. Won Locus Award.
- **Magic System:** Jade grants six disciplines — Strength (physical power), Steel (durability), Lightness (speed/agility), Perception (enhanced senses), Deflection (redirecting attacks), and Channeling (projecting jade energy offensively). Requires genetic predisposition AND years of training. Wearing too much jade without training drives you mad.
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM-HIGH. Green Bones specialize in certain disciplines. Some are Fists (combat), some are Fingers (infiltration). A drug called "shine" lets untrained people use jade temporarily with side effects.
- **Progression:** Yes — characters train, gain more jade, refine techniques.
- **Power/Society:** The jade makes warriors powerful but not invincible. Guns, bombs, and numbers still matter. Political power and jade power intertwine.
- **Tone:** "Godfather with magic" — family crime drama with martial arts.
- **Why for you:** Tight magic system where more jade = more power but also more vulnerability. The disciplines interact interestingly.
- **Audible:** Excellent reviews.

**3. House of Blades (Traveler's Gate #1)** — Will Wight
- **Series:** 3 books + short story collection, complete
- **Magic System:** Travelers can access Territories — pocket dimensions that grant different powers. 11 known Territories, each with distinct abilities:
  - *Valinhall:* House of Blades — gain items and abilities by conquering rooms (steel armor, chains, ghost blades, Nye essence for stealth)
  - *Elysia:* Light powers, healing, considered strongest
  - *Ragnarus:* Blood sacrifice, pain for power
  - *Avernus:* Psychic birds, precognition
  - *Asphodel:* Plant-based powers, mist/fear manipulation
  - And 6+ more...
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Each Territory grants completely different power sets. The protagonist uses Valinhall, which is a dungeon-crawl style progression — clear a room, gain a power.
- **Progression:** YES. This is Will Wight before Cradle. Similar DNA — underdog protagonist must train to catch up.
- **Tone:** Light, fast-paced, action-focused.
- **Why for you:** Same author you liked, different magic system. The Territory variety is like having different "classes" with entirely different mechanics.
- **Audible:** Travis Baldree narrates (same as Cradle).

**4. Forging Divinity (War of Broken Mirrors #1)** — Andrew Rowe
- **Series:** 3 books, complete. Same universe as Arcane Ascension.
- **Magic System:** Dominion Sorcery — casters fuel spells from their own bodies:
  - *Flame Sorcery:* Uses body heat
  - *Sight Sorcery:* Uses eyesight (creates illusions at cost of vision)
  - *Knowledge Sorcery:* Extracts information from things you touch
  - *Metal Sorcery:* Manipulates existing metal's properties
  - *Protection Sorcery:* Creates shields
  - Plus: Core magic (separate system), living gods with their own powers
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Different dominions combo differently. Efficiency improves with practice. Some characters have multiple dominions.
- **Progression:** Yes, though less emphasized than Arcane Ascension.
- **Tone:** More traditional fantasy, political intrigue, heist elements.
- **Why for you:** Andrew Rowe is known for crunchy magic systems. This is his most "hard magic" series — the reader can understand and anticipate what characters will do.
- **Audible:** Available.

---

### TIER 2: Strong Magic Systems, Complete

**5. Knightmare Arcanist (Frith Chronicles #1)** — Shami Stovall
- **Series:** 8 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Bond with a mythical creature to gain powers based on that creature:
  - *Phoenix arcanist:* Fire manipulation, healing
  - *Hydra arcanist:* Poison, regeneration
  - *Knightmare arcanist:* Shadow/darkness manipulation (rare, feared)
  - *Unicorn arcanist:* Purification, light
  - Dozens of creature types, each with different power sets
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Your creature determines your "class." Progression is tied to your creature's growth. You can't change creatures — choice is permanent.
- **Progression:** YES. Academy setting. Training develops both arcanist and creature.
- **Tone:** Light adventure, younger protagonist, found family themes.
- **Why for you:** Clear creature-to-power mapping. Very game-like in structure. Each creature type is essentially a build path.
- **Audible:** Available.

**6. The Mask of Mirrors (Rook & Rose #1)** — M.A. Carrick
- **Series:** 3 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Three distinct systems coexisting:
  - *Numinatria:* Sacred geometry magic — draw precise geometric patterns with numbers 0-10, each number has specific meanings, creates "circuit board" effects. Very structured, almost programming-like.
  - *Pattern:* Tarot-like divination — reading destiny, not just seeing the future but potentially influencing it.
  - *Imbuing:* Enchanting objects with power.
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Characters typically use one system. The systems come from different cultures with different philosophies (ordered vs. intuitive).
- **Progression:** Some — characters refine their skills.
- **Tone:** Intrigue, con artists, political scheming. Venetian-inspired setting.
- **Why for you:** The numinatria system is fascinating — the authors literally used compass and drafting tools to design it. Sacred geometry as programming.
- **Caveat:** Less action-focused than others. More heist/intrigue.
- **Audible:** Available.

**7. The Poppy War** — R.F. Kuang
- **Series:** 3 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Shamanism — channel gods through altered states (meditation, psychedelic drugs). Each god grants different powers:
  - *Phoenix:* Fire, destruction (protagonist's power)
  - *Dragon:* Wind/water
  - *Tortoise:* Earth, stability
  - *Other pantheon members:* Various powers
  - Cost: The gods can overwhelm your will. Using power risks losing yourself to the god.
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. You're bound to one god. The variety is in how you negotiate with/resist that god.
- **Progression:** YES. Rin starts untrained, develops through the series.
- **Tone:** DARK. Military fantasy inspired by Second Sino-Japanese War. Grimdark. War crimes. Genocide.
- **Why for you:** Interesting cost system — power requires surrendering control. The Phoenix doesn't just give fire; it wants to burn everything.
- **Caveat:** Very dark. If you want the magic system without the heaviness, this may not be ideal.
- **Audible:** Complete trilogy available as bundle.

**8. Super Powereds: Year 1** — Drew Hayes
- **Series:** 4 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Superpowers — but with structured categories and government oversight. People are either Supers (control their powers) or Powereds (cannot control). Powers include:
  - Energy manipulation, telepathy, super strength, density control, technopathy, luck manipulation, etc.
  - Each power has specific applications and limitations
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Large cast with diverse powers. Characters learn to use their powers creatively over four years of training.
- **Power/Society:** The DVA (Department of Variant Human Affairs) oversees all heroes. Licensed heroes only. Rigorous certification program — less than 10 of 40+ students graduate. Two-year internship required. Regular oversight and evaluation. Heroes can lose certification for negligence.
- **Progression:** YES. Superhero academy — four years of training, developing powers, learning tactics.
- **Tone:** Light, found family, underdog protagonists.
- **Why for you:** Addresses your concern about power/society through institutional framework rather than societal collapse. Not as dark as Worm, but powers are regulated and controlled.
- **Audible:** Available, well-reviewed. Long books (Year 1 is ~25 hours).

---

### TIER 3: Interesting Options

**9. Worm** — Wildbow
- **Series:** Complete web serial (1.68 million words)
- **Magic System:** Powers ("parahuman abilities") manifest from traumatic "trigger events." Thousands of unique powers, categorized into:
  - *Mover:* Movement powers
  - *Shaker:* Area effects
  - *Brute:* Strength/durability
  - *Breaker:* State-changing
  - *Master:* Minion control
  - *Tinker:* Technology creation
  - *Blaster:* Ranged attacks
  - *Thinker:* Mental enhancement
  - *Striker:* Touch-based
  - *Changer:* Body modification
  - *Trump:* Power manipulation
  - *Stranger:* Stealth/perception
- **Build Variety:** EXTREMELY HIGH. The protagonist controls insects — seems weak but she becomes terrifying through creative application. Every character has a unique power.
- **Power/Society:** THIS IS THE SERIES FOR YOUR CONCERN. Powers are actively causing society to collapse. The "Endbringers" (kaiju-level threats) attack regularly. The source of powers is an Eldritch entity that WANTS conflict. Heroes compromise constantly. Villains are sometimes necessary. The whole genre is deconstructed.
- **Progression:** YES. Taylor goes from bullied teen to one of the most dangerous people alive.
- **Tone:** DARK. The darkest on this list. But not nihilistic — characters fight to save what they can.
- **Why for you:** Takes "why don't powers destroy society?" completely seriously. The answer is: they are, slowly, and everyone is desperately trying to hold things together.
- **CAVEAT — Audible:** NO official audiobook. Fan-made audiobook project exists (free at audioworm.rein-online.org). Also a full-cast podcast version. But you cannot use Audible credits for this.
- **Alternative:** Read free on parahumans.wordpress.com, or use fan audiobook separately.

**10. Beware of Chicken** — Casualfarmer
- **Series:** 5 audiobooks, ongoing (but substantial content exists)
- **Magic System:** Cultivation (xianxia) — but played for comedy and slice-of-life. Standard cultivation tiers (Initiate, Profound, etc.) but the protagonist accidentally cultivates through farming and being nice to his animals. His farm animals also cultivate and gain powers.
  - Qi flows through farming, cooking, community
  - The rooster becomes a martial arts master
  - The fish becomes a healer
  - The pig becomes... a pig, but a cultivated one
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Standard cultivation paths exist in the world, but the protagonist subverts them entirely.
- **Progression:** YES, but backwards — he progresses by NOT trying to progress. His farm passively accumulates power.
- **Tone:** COZY. Slice of life. Wholesome. Funny.
- **Why for you:** Palette cleanser from darker options. Still has cultivation mechanics, just approached from a completely different angle. If you're tired of ruthless cultivators, this is the antidote.
- **Audible:** Travis Baldree narrates (same as Cradle). Books 1-5 available.
- **Caveat:** Ongoing, not complete. But 5 books is substantial.

**11. The Enchanter (Journals of Evander Tailor #1)** — Tobias Begley
- **Series:** 4 books (quadrilogy), complete
- **Magic System:** Academy magic with focus on crafting/enchanting. The protagonist is gifted at enchanting — creating magical items, inscriptions, and artifacts. Magic follows logical rules that can be studied and applied.
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Different magical disciplines exist at the academy. Enchanting is the focus.
- **Progression:** YES. Academy setting, student to master arc.
- **Tone:** Light, school problems, bullies, taking too many classes.
- **Why for you:** If you're interested in the "crafting" side of magic systems — how items are made, how enchantments work, the logic of magical engineering.
- **Audible:** Available.

**12. My Best Friend is an Eldritch Horror** — Actus
- **Series:** 6 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Academy magic where the protagonist accidentally bonds with an Eldritch entity named "Henry." He can access Void magic (rare, forbidden) while hiding his companion's true nature. Standard magical disciplines exist alongside his unique situation.
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. The protagonist has a unique path; other students have more standard magical development.
- **Progression:** YES. Magic academy, grows from student to powerful mage.
- **Tone:** Mix of slice-of-life, comedy, and action. Not grimdark.
- **Why for you:** Unique twist on academy progression. The "forbidden power you must hide" trope done interestingly.
- **CAVEAT:** Described as "LitRPG" in some listings. It may have some game-like elements, though reviews suggest it's lighter on stats than typical LitRPG. Worth checking a sample before committing.
- **Audible:** Complete 6-book bundle available.

---

## Summary Table

## Notes on Your Specific Interests

**For build-heavy game design inspiration:**
- Lightbringer (color combinations, specializations)
- Traveler's Gate (11 distinct "classes")
- Frith Chronicles (creature = build path)
- Worm (power categorization, creative application)

**For crafting/enchanting:**
- The Enchanter
- War of Broken Mirrors (includes item creation)
- Rook & Rose (numinatria is almost like magical programming)

**For power/society dynamics:**
- Worm (takes it most seriously — powers are destroying civilization)
- Super Powereds (institutional control, licensing, oversight)
- Green Bone Saga (jade as political/economic power)

**For slice-of-life/lighter tone:**
- Beware of Chicken
- Frith Chronicles
- Super Powereds

Based on my search, I found several examples of superhero stories featuring government oversight and registration of heroes, though the results primarily cover comic book series rather than prose novels. Here's what I found:

## Super Registration Act Trope

The concept often involves a government-sponsored system "complete with Hero Insurance," though in most cases the law is portrayed as antagonistic, designed to "prohibit superheroes from using their powers recklessly (or usually at all)."

## Notable Comic Series Examples

**Marvel's Civil War:**
After an explosive battle between the New Warriors and Nitro left hundreds dead, Congress introduced the Superhuman Registration Act. Iron Man became the law's biggest supporter, while Captain America strongly objected, leading the heroes of the Marvel Universe to go to war with one another.(no content)The Act enables the government to monitor all powered individuals and is drafted to facilitate the government's licensing and/or employment of individuals who are actively using their powers. The powered individual must fulfill some requirements or meet some criteria before they are allowed to fully use their abilities and gain legal authorization to continue to use their abilities to fight crime.

**Powers (by Bendis &amp; Oeming):**
In the Powers series, superheroes had to register with the government in order to operate. After Super Shock, the world's most trusted superhero, goes on a massive worldwide killing spree, the US government prohibited super-beings from using their powers and operating as superheroes.

**Astro City:**
In Kurt Busiek's Astro City Vol. 2 #6-9, the registration of super-humans is mandated by the city's Mayor Stevenson. Federal E.A.G.L.E. agents enforce the new requirement, which is opposed by many active super-heroes, with the prominent hero Winged Victory making outspoken statements opposing registration.(no content)Similar acts have been used as literary devices in "Uncanny X-Men, DC: The New Frontier, Powers, Watchmen, The Incredibles, and Astro City."

If you're looking for a specific **prose novel series** (rather than comics) with these themes, let me know and I can search more specifically for that.

Here are some excellent progression fantasy audiobook recommendations with interesting magic systems and build variety:

## Top Recommendations

### **Cradle Series** by Will Wight
The Cradle series follows the story of Lindon, a lowly "unsouled" youth who is deemed worthless by his society due to his lack of magic. In this world, magic is everything, and those who possess it are considered superior to those who don't. However, Lindon refuses to give up and embarks on a journey to become a powerful fighter and prove his worth.(no content)The series is known for its imaginative world-building, intricate magic system, and engaging characters. The magic system is based on the manipulation of vital aura, a type of energy that flows through all living things.

### **Arcane Ascension Series** by Andrew Rowe
This series has a good mix of magic school, dungeon crawling, puzzle-solving, and a hint of RPG elements integrated into the world, for example, a class-like system called "attunements" that each character is bound to.(no content)The series also has an incredible audiobook version narrated by Nick Podehl. It is also part of a greater universe, including the War of Broken Mirrors and the Weapon and Wielders books.

### **Mage Errant Series** by John Bierce
This series is filled with a great cast of characters, a unique magic system, dungeon crawling, and of course, lots and lots of training. If you enjoy great character building, fun action sequences, huge monsters, with a splash of romance, you're sure to enjoy this series.

### **All the Skills**
All the Skills is an epic progression-fantasy story featuring a unique card-based magic system. With a fun and gripping story, a likable main character, great world-building, and an excellent performance by narrator Luke Daniels, this audiobook is well worth a listen.

### **Iron Prince** (Warformed: Stormweaver) by Bryce O'Connor &amp; Luke Chmilenko
This is book 1 in the Warformed: Stormweaver series, sitting at 1112 pages and 33 hours and 55 minutes in audiobook format. Unlike other books, this one is Science Fiction Progression Fantasy, filled with futuristic arena combat, a military academy setting where power is everything, and a protagonist that doesn't know the word "quit".

### **Knightmare Arcanist** by Shami Stovall
Set in a unique world where everyone gains magical powers based on the mythical creature they bond to. Phoenix arcanists have fire and healing, whereas hydra arcanists have poison and regeneration—the stronger the creature, the more amazing the powers. Volke Savan bonds with a creature of shadow—a knightmare—and soon learns that his magic progresses based on his training and spiritual cultivation.

### **He Who Fights with Monsters**
The story of Jason, a man transported into a game-like world, is filled with captivating game mechanics, power-ups, and an array of fascinating creatures. Heath Miller's narration complements Shirtaloon's storytelling, making each level-up, skill gain, and boss fight feel truly momentous.

Based on the search results, here are some notable progression fantasy books featuring crafting, enchanting, and artificer themes:

## Highly Recommended Crafting/Enchanter Series

### **The Enchanter by Tobias Begley**
If you've read the Arcane Ascension series and loved Corin's approach to life, this is highly recommended. Similarly, if you've read Mother of Learning and appreciated Zorian, the same recommendation applies.(no content)The MC, Evander Tailor, is gifted and gets to learn magic at a magic school, where he faces typical school-like problems and some spicier challenges.(no content)The crafting and magic system are big draws, but the human element really takes it home.

### **Arcane Ascension Series (Andrew Rowe)**
A Sandersonian-esque approach to fantasy with labyrinthine towers where young people train to earn magical attunements. The main character's attunement turns out to be Enchanter, similar to the concept in Skyrim.(no content)The Enchanting attunement is somewhat looked down upon by his martial family, as it's deemed too passive and indirect for combat.

### **Arcane Artificer (Dren's Den Book 1)** - Andrew Karevik
In the crafting village of Arthursberg, Dren discovers an Artificer's workshop and is granted the Artificer Class at Level 1, thrust into a world where creativity meets combat.(no content)He must rebuild himself by constructing mechanical limbs, but resources are scarce and the only way to get them is by diving into dungeons.

### **Emerilia Series**
Emerilia is built on MMO-inspired mechanics where forging and building are central to character advancement. Characters progress by crafting weapons, enchanting gear, and managing resources, creating a world that feels alive and player-driven.

### **Knights &amp; Magic**
This is about an artificer who designs new models of magic-powered robots for the kingdom military. There's a lot of focus on R&amp;D, and the protagonist's designs are revolutionary but he needs help from experienced technicians to make them practical.

### **Mage Errant by John Bierce**
This series follows Hugh of Emblin, a struggling mage-in-training who discovers hidden potential under the mentorship of an eccentric teacher. Set within a magical academy with imaginative world-building and a unique magical "Labyrinth."

Based on my search, here's what I found about **Corpies** by Drew Hayes:

## Overview

Corpies is the first spin-off novel from the Super Powereds series by Drew Hayes.(no content)The series reading order is: Super Powereds: Year 1, Super Powereds: Year 2, then the spinoff Corpies, followed by Super Powereds: Year 3 and Year 4.

## Plot Summary

Titan was one of the nation's most loved and respected Heroes, until an infidelity scandal tore his image and family apart. After decades spent out of the limelight, Owen Daniels has decided to take up the mantle of Titan once again to try and make amends for his years away. Unfortunately, the Titan Scandal is still common knowledge, and no Hero team wants such a polarizing figure.(no content)With no other options, Owen is forced to take a job overseeing a group of corpies, corporate-sponsored Supers who do rescue work… as long as there are cameras around. Between a team that doesn't want him, fellow Heroes who don't trust him, and a nation that might not be ready to forgive the sins of the past, the return of Titan could prove even harder than the scandal that drove him away.(no content)A mysterious enemy is attacking Heroes and growing steadily stronger. An enemy that only the once-legendary Titan might be able to stop. If he can manage to stick around this time.

## Series Status

Corpies is listed as Book 5 of 5 in the Super Powereds series on Amazon, though chronologically it takes place between Year 2 and Year 3. "Corpies" is best read between Super Powereds books 2 and 3, as reviewers recommend. It shows the other side of the coin for Supers who don't get into the HCP: the corporate-sponsored heroes who can still help with emergency services but aren't permitted to fight bad guys.

## Author

Drew Hayes graduated from Texas Tech with a degree in English. He is the author of many books, including NPCs and The Utterly Uninteresting and Unadventurous Tales of Fred, the Vampire Accountant. He lives in Texas.

The Super Powereds main series (Years 1-4) is complete, and Corpies serves as a standalone spinoff that expands the universe.

Here's what I found about the **Grimnoir Chronicles** by Larry Correia:

## Overview
Larry Correia is The New York Times best-selling author of the Grimnoir Chronicles alternate history trilogy.(no content)The Grimnoir Chronicles are a series of books that detail an alternate 1930s where people born with magical abilities called Actives have existed for the last century. Magic began manifesting in 1849.

## The Magic System &amp; Powers
Only a handful of people in the world know that mankind's magic comes from a living creature, and it is a refugee from another universe. The Power showed up here in the 1850s because it was running from something.(no content)The Grimnoir Society's mission is to protect people with magic, and they've done so - successfully and in secret - since the mysterious arrival of the Power in the 1850s.

The main character, Jake Sullivan, possesses raw magical talent and the ability to make objects in his vicinity light as a feather or as heavy as depleted uranium, all with a magical thought.(no content)Jake's talent is gravity spiking.

Another character, Faye, is a young farm girl who can teleport across great distances.(no content)First, we get glimpses and small pieces of information, then more and more and we end up with a pretty complete picture of how the magic works, powers fighting to dominate it, and their motivation. The author had it thought through before he finished the first volume.

## The Complete Trilogy
The three main books are:
1. **Hard Magic** (Book I) - Won the Audie Award for Paranormal in 2012.
2. **Spellbound** (Book II) - Won the Audie Award for Paranormal in 2013.
3. **Warbound** (Book III)

There's also a brand-new Grimnoir Chronicles story written exclusively for Audible, set in 1937 – four years after the Grimnoir Society defeated the magical alien force known as The Power. "Heavy" Jake Sullivan is summoned by his oddest ally, Dr. Wells, to stop the bombing of a new ultra-luxury airship. Amid the glitz, the gambling, and the high-society types, Sullivan races time to hunt for the saboteur.

## Audiobooks
Bronson Pinchot's narration of the audiobook was brilliant. He took the whole production to a higher level. He easily managed all those characters with their different ethnicities and education levels — it was delightful, and was one of the best audiobook performances.(no content)Bronson Pinchot did a great job narrating the series.

The audiobooks are available on Audible and Amazon.

## Series Overview

The Art of the Adept series has 8 entries.(no content)The series includes books The Choice of Magic (Art of the Adept, #1), Secrets and Spellcraft (Art of the Adept, #2), Scholar of Magic, and several more.

## Audiobook Availability

The audiobooks are narrated by Tim Gerard Reynolds and published by Podium Audio. The series is available on Audible (US, UK, and Australia).

## Magic System &amp; Story

The series features a unique contrast between two magical traditions:

"The ancient magic of wizards was anything but dark. It was the enlightenment that lifted humanity from the squalor of superstition, and the worship of fell spirits and capricious gods, but those days are gone. The shining glory of the sorcerers burned away the subtlety of wisdom, replacing it with easy power, held only in the hands of the elite - a new age built upon the elemental supremacy of aristocrats and the ignorance of the masses."(no content)But this will change, for the greatest power comes with knowledge, and the deeper teachings of wizardry have not been utterly lost. The last wizard of the old tradition still survives in solitude, nursing tired grudges and waiting for death. His passing might have gone unnoticed, but for the imposition of a youth too stubborn to accept his refusal to take an apprentice. With a new student comes new hope, and that hope has caused old powers to stir again.

## Character Progression

Will's journey from naïve apprentice to a mature wizard is almost complete, and his ever-growing mastery has reached unseen heights. But his power does not exist in a vacuum. His rising star threatens to eclipse the existing powers and a new balance must be found, one that either accepts his primacy or extinguishes his light.

## Reader Reception

There was some great expansion of magic in this book too and some fun reveals. The book is really well written and also well paced. The "battle" scenes were rich, but not overly frequent so there was time spent on character development and expansion of magic.

## Series Overview
Terry Mancour is a New York Times Best-Selling Author who has written more than 30 books, under his own name and pseudonyms, including the Spellmonger Series (more than 20 books and growing).

## Magic System
Starting with "Spellmonger", Terry Mancour builds an exquisite world set in a feudal society. The systems of magic, the interactions between just-different-enough races of magical folk, and the extraordinary wit and humor in the main characters make this series highly regarded.

The magic system involves various types of practitioners, including:
- Warmages who serve in professional capacities, and village spellmongers who practice in remote areas of the world of Callidore.
- Magical gemstones called irionite that can be used to raise magi to become High Magi.
- Various magical practitioners including High Magi, hedgemagi, witches and footwizards.

## Completion Status
The author has plotted the Spellmonger Series for at least thirty books, in addition to his Spellmonger Cadet (young adult) series, stand-alone novels, and short stories.(no content)The series currently includes 17 main numbered books plus side stories, with the most recent being "Practical Adept (2024)", "The Golden Goblin (2025)", and "The Talon and the Flame (2025)". The series is **not yet complete** and continues to grow.

## Audiobooks
The audiobooks are narrated by John Lee, whose smooth, strong, and clear voice guides listeners through the fantastical world of Callidore with impeccable pacing and pronunciation.(no content)The series is a New York Times audiobook and Audible best-selling series.(no content)Spellmonger was nominated for the 2018 Audie Award for Best Fantasy for its audiobook.

Here's what I found about the magic system in Tamora Pierce's Circle of Magic series:

## Magic System Overview

In this universe, there are two types of magic: academic magic and ambient magic.

### Ambient Magic

Ambient Magic is a form of magic known only in the Circle Universe.(no content)The major quality of ambient magic is that the strength of the power is from the outside world, and not the inside of the mage, like academic magic. Ambient magic doesn't draw on the mage's self-created power like Academic Magic, but from the surroundings and craft items of the mage.(no content)It is not as well known as the traditional Academic Magic, and in fact is only one fourth times as common as academic magic. Ambient magic takes different forms depending on the mage and the craft he or she performs—common ones include stone, carpentry, healing, cooking, thread and needlework, pottery, fire, and weather.(no content)As ambient magic has a tendency to break free of the user and cause havoc if not properly controlled, it is imperative that a student find an accredited teacher. Ambient mages can be accredited through Winding Circle or the University of Lightsbridge.

### Academic Magic

Academic magic is a form of magic in the Emelan Universe. It is very similar to the Gift, a type of magic in the Tortallan Universe, as it is directly linked to the power vested in the user and not in the surrounding world, as opposed to ambient magic. It usually requires incantations and physical catalysts in order to perform it.(no content)The three signs of an academic mage are telekinesis (moving objects with one's mind), creating images in fire, and causing objects to glow. Most academic mages display at least one of these talents at a young age.

### Can Mages Have Both?

It is possible to possess both the academic and ambient forms of magic. However, while ambient mages can learn academic magic and often apply its principles to their work, academic mages do not possess the inherent ability to learn ambient magic. Ambient magic is known to block academic magic when it is not controlled.(no content)Trisana Chandler is an ambient weather mage who taught herself academic magic.

### Training Locations

It is a common misconception that all academic mages go to Lightsbridge, and all ambient mages go to Winding Circle. It is just a different sort of life, as Winding Circle is mostly temple life, while Lightsbridge is university life.

### The Four Main Characters

In Book 1, gifted young weaver Sandry meets Briar, a former thief with a way with plants; Daja, an outcast gifted at metalcraft; and Tris, whose connection with the weather unsettles everyone, including herself.

... [2 more lines]</code></pre>

Here's what I found about the **Vita Nostra** audiobook by Marina and Sergey Dyachenko:

## Audiobook Details

The audiobook is narrated by Jessica Ball and was translated by Julia Meitov Hersey, published by HarperCollins Publishers Limited.(no content)It's described as "the definitive English language translation of the internationally bestselling Russian novel—a brilliant dark fantasy" combining psychological suspense, enchantment, and terror.

## About the Book

Sasha Samokhina meets the mysterious Farit Kozhennikov while on holiday. She is asked to undertake strange tasks and is rewarded with golden coins. Eventually, Farit instructs her to travel to a remote village and use her gold to gain entrance to the Institute of Special Technologies. Sasha quickly discovers this is no ordinary school.(no content)The books are impossible to read, the lessons obscure to the point of maddening, and the work refuses memorization. Using terror and coercion to keep students in line, the school does not punish them for their transgressions and failures; instead, their families pay a terrible price.

## Where to Listen

The audiobook is available on multiple platforms:
- **Audible** (audible.com)
- **Google Play Books**
- **Everand** (formerly Scribd)
- **OverDrive** (through libraries)
- **Barnes &amp; Noble**

## The Series

There is a sequel that "takes readers to the next stage in Sasha Samokhina's journey in a richly imagined world of dark academia in which grammar is magic—and not all magic is good."

## About the Authors

Marina and Sergey Dyachenko, a former actress and a former psychiatrist, are co-authors of over thirty novels and numerous short stories and screenplays. They were born in Ukraine and moved to California in 2013. They are recipients of the Award for Best Authors (Eurocon 2005), Prix Planete SF des blogueurs (2020), Grand Prix de l'Imaginaire (2020) and of the Science Fiction and Fantasy Rosetta Awards (2021). Sergey Dyachenko passed away in 2022.

## The Trilogy

The entire #1 New York Times bestselling Magicians trilogy includes The Magicians, The Magician King, and The Magician's Land.

## Audiobook Details

Actor and narrator Mark Bramhall brings Quentin Coldwater to life throughout the trilogy, easily walking through reality and fantasy as this young man struggles with the disappointment of learning that things aren't as magical as he'd hoped.(no content)Bramhall's voice and narrative style have won him many accolades, including more than 30 AudioFile Earphones Awards, and he's narrated alongside greats like Meryl Streep in the full-cast recording of Charlotte's Web.

## About the Magic System &amp; Story

The story follows protagonist Quentin Coldwater, a complicated, brilliant, and miserable young man, as he unexpectedly gets admitted to an exclusive, and very secret, college of magic and goes through typical college experiences.(no content)Instead of Princeton, he finds himself invited to study at Brakebills – a secret college of modern-day sorcerers.(no content)The series explores the dark side of magic as seen through real people performing it, with all their impulsive desires and volatile emotions.

Based on the search results, here's what I found about the Vita Nostra series:

## English Language Series

The English (and international) version of the Vita Nostra series contains two books (as of 2022) which are books 1 and 4 of the Russian series "Метаморфозы" (Metamorphosis).

The current English books are:
1. **Vita Nostra** - Vita Nostra was published in 2007. Julia Meitov Hersey's translation was published by HarperCollins Publishers in November 2018.

2. **Assassin of Reality** - The latest book, Assassin of Reality (Book 2), was published in March 2023.(no content)It is the sequel to 2007 novel Vita Nostra. The English translation was published in 2023.

3. **School of Shards** - School of Shards is described as "the Final Chapter of the Vita Nostra Trilogy", making it Book 3 in the series.

## Original Russian "Metamorphosis" Cycle

Vita Nostra was published in 2007. It was the first novel in the thematically related "Metamorphosis" cycle.(no content)Digital, or Brevis Est, (2009) and Migrant, or Brevi Finietur, a work of science fiction, continue the cycle.

So the complete picture is:
- **Russian Metamorphosis cycle**: 4 books
- **English Vita Nostra series**: 3 books (a trilogy), with School of Shards being the final book

One reviewer noted being "a bit heartbroken I might have to wait another few years for the last book in the trilogy."

## Progression Fantasy with Runic Magic

This story features a Runic-Tattoo Wizard/Spellblade in a world of sorcerers, with an exceptional MC and some initial slow burn elements, inspired by epics such as Azarinth Healer.(no content)Kaius just wanted to unlock his class - instead, he restarted the apocalypse. ### Other Progression Fantasy with Crafting Elements

**Emerilia** is built on MMO-inspired mechanics where forging and building are central to character advancement. Characters progress by crafting weapons, enchanting gear, and managing resources. For fans of MMO-style progression and detailed systems, Emerilia is a strong choice among the best progression fantasy series with crafting depth.(no content)In **The Ten Realms**, crafting is essential to survival and growth. Erik and Rugrat forge weapons, brew potions, and manage supply chains that matter as much as combat.

## Story Synopsis
Nate is a kid from Sydney, Australia who spends his free time indulging in his one true love - art. Graffiti specifically. That is until his 'hobby' catapults him into a new world filled with danger and magic. Finding himself alone in a forest that is clearly not on Earth, he must learn to navigate this new world and more importantly, the System that governs it.(no content)Armed with nothing but his trusty penknife and a Legendary Class, Nate will fend for his life. He'll conquer dungeons, discover runes and be drawn into battles against enemies he didn't even know he had, all while making new friends along the way. Torn between returning to his old life and the friends he left behind, or making a new home in this world filled with magic, he will have to decide where his heart truly lies.

## Series Status: **Incomplete** (3 of 7 planned books published)

### Published Books:
The first novel, *The Lies of Locke Lamora*, was published in June 2006. The next two novels in the series, *Red Seas Under Red Skies* and *The Republic of Thieves*, were published in 2007 and 2013, respectively.

### Planned Future Books:
*The Thorn of Emberlain*, *The Ministry of Necessity*, *The Mage and the Master Spy*, and *Inherit the Night* are projected to conclude the series.(no content)The author's website confirms the Gentleman Bastard Sequence will consist of seven novels total.

### Latest Updates (August 2024):
While attending the World Science Fiction Convention in Glasgow, Scotland, Lynch shared an update on his Gentleman Bastard series. The author revealed that he'll be releasing three novellas ahead of *The Thorn of Emberlain* — and it sounds like they're fairly fleshed out already.(no content)The linked sequence of the 3 Gentleman Bastard novellas will be called *The Road to Emberlain*, bridging the gap between the series's third and fourth books.(no content)Lynch confirmed that each novella will be around 40,000 words.

### Recent Content:
In October 2024, the first half of the short story "Locke Lamora and the Bottled Serpent" was published in Grimdark Magazine #40, with the remainder published in #41 in January 2025.

### Book 4 Status:
Scott finished a draft of the next Gentleman Bastard novel, *The Thorn of Emberlain*, at the end of May 2019.(no content)The fourth Gentleman Bastard book doesn't have a release date just yet, but we can rest assured that it's still in the works.

In summary, fans have been waiting over 11 years since the last main novel, but Lynch appears to be actively working on the series with novellas and the upcoming fourth book.

## The Founders Trilogy by Robert Jackson Bennett

### Overview

Foundryside is a 2018 fantasy novel by Robert Jackson Bennett. It was first published by Crown Publishing Group on August 21, 2018. It is the first book in a trilogy that includes Shorefall (2020) and Locklands (2022).(no content)The author of the Divine Cities trilogy (a nominee for Best Series at the 2018 Hugo Awards) begins a new trilogy that's as fun to read as its world is well-imagined.

### The Scriving Magic System

In the city of Tevanne, "scriving" — the systematization and mass production of sigils — has enabled the industrialization of magic.(no content)Scriving constitutes the central magic system in Foundryside, wherein skilled artisans known as scrivers inscribe sigils—hieroglyphic symbols representing lexical definitions—onto man-made objects to reprogram their inherent understanding of physical laws.(no content)Scriving is magic that can imbue inanimate objects with sentience, and argue reality into working in ways it was not intended.

### Examples of Scriving in Practice

Similar scriving is used in the weapons of the elite class such as for example, a rapier. It can be scrived to amplify its gravity so that it believes it is being wielded with the force of ten men and will effortlessly cut through a person or punch through solid walls. Carriage wheels can be made to roll uphill without needing horses, wood can be scrived with the sigil for clay, making it inherently softer and easier to carve. The applications are endless and indeed very varied throughout the book.

### Critical Reception

The series has been praised extensively for its innovative approach:

- "Foundryside pulls you in with fast-paced heists, then knocks you down with its innovative magic system. Fun, thoughtful, and thrilling from cover to cover, it's sword-and-sorcery meets computer programming."

- The Verge described it as "essentially a cyberpunk novel, trapped in the clothes of an epic fantasy", and "pressingly modern and relevant."

- "The best epic fantasy of the year is also the best cyberpunk of the year. How often do you get to say that?"

### Story &amp; Characters

## Overview

The Threadbare books are a LitRPG outing by Andrew Seiple, started in Fall 2017, and then released to online stores.(no content)Threadbare is the main character of the Threadbare trilogy. He is a twelve-inch-tall greater toy golem in the form of an old threadbare teddy bear who will do anything to protect his friends.

## The Complete Series (6 Books)

Volumes 4-6 have been added to complete the story. The full series includes:

5. **The Phantom of the Lop Ear** (Volume 5)
6. **An End to All Tails** (Volume 6)

## Plot Summary

Meet Threadbare. He is twelve inches tall, full of fluff, and really, really bad at being a hero. Magically animated and discarded by his maker as a failed experiment, he is saved by a little girl. But she's got problems of her own, and he might not be able to help her. Fortunately for the little golem, he's quick to find allies, learn skills, gain levels, and survive horrible predicaments. Which is good, because his creator has a whole lot of enemies.(no content)Threadbare follows the journey of the eponymous bear's quest to try and find and save the daughter of his creator and his best friend - Cecelia Gearheart.

## Key Features

- Pun-Based Titles for all six volumes, and Crafting-based Theme Naming for the first two books.
- A masterful blend of laugh-out-loud humor and genuinely touching moments of found family. Well-integrated LitRPG mechanics that drive a satisfying progression.
- Greater Golems, like Threadbare, can acquire Jobs and improve their skills.
