I have comprehensive research now. Let me compile 12 new recommendations focused on interesting magic systems, crafting/enchanting, and build variety.

---

## 12 More Recommendations: Magic Systems, Crafting & Build Variety

---

### CRAFTING/ENCHANTING FOCUS

**1. Foundryside (The Founders Trilogy #1)** — Robert Jackson Bennett
- **Series:** 3 books, complete (Foundryside, Shorefall, Locklands)
- **Magic System:** Scriving — essentially programming reality. Scrivers inscribe sigils onto objects to "convince" them to behave differently:
  - A rapier can be scrived to believe it's being swung with the force of ten men
  - Wheels can be convinced gravity pulls them uphill
  - Wood can believe it's soft like clay
  - The magic follows logical rules like code — if-then statements, loops, permissions
- **Build Variety:** Different scrivers specialize in different applications. The protagonist has a unique ability to "hear" objects and understand their scriving.
- **Progression:** Yes — characters develop their understanding and create more complex scrivings.
- **Tone:** Heist/cyberpunk energy in a fantasy setting. "Sword-and-sorcery meets computer programming."
- **Why for you:** Scriving is basically magical programming. If you design game systems, this magic system will feel very familiar — it's about understanding rules and exploiting them creatively.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Tara Sands. Complete trilogy available.

**2. Art of the Adept (The Choice of Magic #1)** — Michael G. Manning
- **Series:** 5 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Contrasts two traditions:
  - *Sorcery:* Easy power, elemental supremacy, aristocratic
  - *Wizardry:* Older tradition, requires deep study, more versatile but harder to learn
  - The protagonist learns the nearly-lost art of wizardry from the last master
- **Build Variety:** Different schools of magic, different approaches to spell construction. Wizardry is about understanding principles rather than rote casting.
- **Progression:** YES. Will goes from naive apprentice to powerful wizard across five books. Training and study are central.
- **Tone:** Traditional fantasy adventure with academy elements.
- **Why for you:** Deep magic system that rewards understanding over raw power. Good for seeing how "study and mastery" progression works.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Tim Gerard Reynolds (excellent). Complete series available.

**3. Six Sacred Swords (Weapons and Wielders #1)** — Andrew Rowe
- **Series:** 3 books out, ongoing (planned 6-7 books, book 4 in progress for 2026)
- **Magic System:** Same universe as Arcane Ascension, but focused on:
  - Legendary weapons with unique properties and personalities
  - Each Sacred Sword has different abilities and requirements
  - Dominion sorcery from War of Broken Mirrors also appears
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. The protagonist Keras has multiple magic types. Each sword encountered has distinct mechanics.
- **Progression:** Yes — collecting and mastering new weapons, developing abilities.
- **Tone:** Light, fun, inspired by Legend of Zelda, Dragon Quest, and JRPGs. Fast-paced adventure.
- **Why for you:** Andrew Rowe wrote this specifically as a "video game in book form." If you liked his magic system design in Arcane Ascension, this explores the same universe from a more action-oriented angle.
- **Caveat:** Ongoing, not complete. But 3 substantial books exist.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Nick Podehl (same as Arcane Ascension).

---

### SUPERHERO / POWER SOCIETY

**4. Hard Magic (Grimnoir Chronicles #1)** — Larry Correia
- **Series:** 3 books, complete (+ new Audible-exclusive novella)
- **Magic System:** Powers appeared in the 1850s from a mysterious alien entity called "The Power." People born with abilities are called Actives. Powers are categorized:
  - *Heavies:* Gravity manipulation
  - *Travelers:* Teleportation
  - *Brutes:* Enhanced strength/durability
  - *Readers:* Telepathy
  - *Mouths:* Voice compulsion
  - *Fades:* Intangibility
  - And many more categories...
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Each Active has one primary power, but application varies widely. The protagonist Jake Sullivan can make things heavy or light.
- **Power/Society:** Set in 1930s alternate history. The Power chose people to give abilities to — why? What does it want? Imperial Japan has weaponized Actives. The US government has registration. Secret societies (Grimnoir) protect Actives.
- **Progression:** Characters develop new applications of their powers, learn the deeper nature of magic.
- **Tone:** Noir/pulp action. Think 1930s detective meets X-Men.
- **Why for you:** Categorized power system with clear rules. Addresses power/society through alt-history lens. Also won Audie Awards for audiobook.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Bronson Pinchot — frequently cited as one of the best narrator performances in fantasy. Won Audie Awards.

**5. Vicious (Villains #1)** — V.E. Schwab
- **Series:** 2 books, complete duology (Vicious, Vengeful)
- **Magic System:** EOs (ExtraOrdinaries) gain powers from near-death experiences. The specific power relates to what you were thinking/feeling when you almost died:
  - Victor: Pain manipulation
  - Eli: Regeneration/immortality
  - Sydney: Resurrection
  - Each power has clear limits and costs
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Each EO has one power, but the variety across characters is high.
- **Power/Society:** The question of whether EOs are "wrong" or "unnatural" is central. One protagonist believes EOs are abominations that should be killed. Society doesn't know EOs exist — it's hidden, but the question of what would happen if they went public lurks.
- **Tone:** Dark, morally grey. Neither protagonist is heroic. It's about villains vs. villains.
- **Why for you:** Tight, focused exploration of what superpowers would actually do to people. Powers have psychological costs.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Jeremy Arthur. Complete duology.

**6. Corpies** — Drew Hayes
- **Series:** 1 book, standalone spinoff (set in Super Powereds universe)
- **Magic System:** Same as Super Powereds — Supers with controlled powers, licensed Heroes, DVA oversight.
- **Unique Angle:** Follows "Corpies" — corporate-sponsored Supers who do rescue work and PR but aren't licensed for combat. Shows the other side of the superhero world.
- **Protagonist:** Titan, a legendary Hero whose career was destroyed by scandal, now trying to rebuild by working with a Corpie team.
- **Power/Society:** Explores the line between Heroes and Corpies, how the licensing system creates different tiers of powered people, and what happens when you're powerful but not "allowed" to fight.
- **Tone:** Lighter than Vicious, still has stakes. Adult characters rather than students.
- **Why for you:** If you liked Super Powereds' handling of power oversight, this shows another facet. Good companion piece.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Kyle McCarley. Available.

---

### UNIQUE MAGIC SYSTEMS

**7. A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic #1)** — V.E. Schwab
- **Series:** 3 books, complete (+ continuation novel The Fragile Threads of Power)
- **Magic System:** Four parallel Londons exist, each with different magic levels:
  - *Grey London:* Our world, no magic
  - *Red London:* Magic flourishes, balanced
  - *White London:* Magic is scarce, fought over viciously
  - *Black London:* Consumed by magic, now sealed away
  - Antari are rare magicians who can travel between worlds using blood magic
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Different types of elemental magic, blood magic for world-travel, artifact magic.
- **Progression:** Characters develop their magic, learn new applications, confront the nature of Black London's corruption.
- **Tone:** Swashbuckling adventure, heist elements, parallel world exploration.
- **Why for you:** The "magic as a resource that different worlds have in different amounts" concept is interesting for worldbuilding. Each London has different rules.
- **Audible:** Multiple narrator options — original (Steven Crossley) or newer versions (Michael Kramer/Kate Reading).

**8. The Magicians** — Lev Grossman
- **Series:** 3 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Academic magic learned at Brakebills, a hidden college:
  - Magic requires precise hand movements adjusted for ambient conditions (weather, location, time)
  - Spells are difficult, dangerous, and require years of study
  - Different magical disciplines (physical magic, illusions, etc.)
  - Also: Fillory, a Narnia-like world with different, older magic
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Students specialize in disciplines. But magic is hard for everyone.
- **Progression:** Quentin goes from student to graduate to... something more complicated.
- **Tone:** DARK. "Harry Potter for adults" but genuinely dark — depression, meaninglessness, the question of what you do when you get everything you wanted and it's not enough.
- **Why for you:** Subverts fantasy tropes hard. Magic doesn't make you happy. What Narnia would actually be like. George R.R. Martin said "The Magicians is to Harry Potter as a shot of Irish whiskey is to a glass of weak tea."
- **Caveat:** The protagonist is deliberately frustrating early on. That's intentional.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Mark Bramhall (30+ AudioFile Earphones Awards).

**9. Sandry's Book (Circle of Magic #1)** — Tamora Pierce
- **Series:** 4 books in original quartet, complete. (11 books total in the Circle Universe)
- **Magic System:** Two distinct types:
  - *Academic Magic:* Traditional learned magic, powered from within, requires incantations. Signs: telekinesis, fire images, glowing objects.
  - *Ambient Magic:* Rare. Power drawn from crafts and the world — thread magic, plant magic, metal magic, weather magic. Must be trained or it breaks free and causes havoc.
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. The four protagonists each have different ambient magic:
  - *Sandry:* Thread/weaving magic
  - *Tris:* Weather magic
  - *Daja:* Metalcraft magic
  - *Briar:* Plant magic
- **Progression:** YES. Students learn to control their dangerous ambient gifts.
- **Tone:** YA, but well-crafted. Found family, academy setting at Winding Circle temple.
- **Why for you:** The ambient/academic distinction is clever — it's about whether power comes from within or from your craft. Each magic type feels genuinely different.
- **Audible:** Full cast audiobook. Available.

**10. Vita Nostra** — Marina & Sergey Dyachenko
- **Series:** 2 books in English, with third (final) coming
- **Magic System:** Language and grammar as reality-altering magic. Students at the Institute of Special Technologies study "specialized subjects" that literally redefine what they are:
  - Textbooks cannot be memorized, only experienced
  - Exercises seem meaningless until they change you
  - Students transform into something not entirely human
  - Grammar becomes the structure of reality itself
- **Build Variety:** LOW in traditional sense — everyone studies the same thing, but transforms differently.
- **Progression:** YES, but terrifying. Sasha doesn't want to progress, but the Institute won't let her stop.
- **Tone:** DARK. Psychological horror meets dark academia. The school uses terror and coercion. Failure means your family suffers.
- **Why for you:** Completely unique magic concept. If you want something that feels genuinely alien and unsettling, this is it. The magic system is mysterious but internally consistent.
- **Caveat:** Not complete in English (book 3 coming). Very dark, not for everyone.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Jessica Ball. Books 1-2 available.

---

### SCI-FI/PROGRESSION HYBRIDS

**11. Iron Prince (Warformed: Stormweaver #1)** — Bryce O'Connor & Luke Chmilenko
- **Series:** 2 books (Iron Prince, Fire and Song), ongoing
- **Magic System:** CADs (Cognitive Assisting Devices) — living weapons that bond with users and evolve based on combat data:
  - Different CAD types: blades, ranged, shields, etc.
  - Users develop combat skills that synergize with their CAD
  - CADs literally grow and change based on how you fight
  - Military academy structure with rankings and competitions
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Your CAD's evolution depends on your fighting style. Different users have vastly different weapon configurations.
- **Progression:** YES. This is pure progression fantasy. The protagonist starts at the absolute bottom (F-rank) and must claw his way up through determination and creative tactics.
- **Tone:** Sci-fi academy, competitive but not grimdark. Underdog story.
- **Why for you:** The CAD system is essentially a living skill tree that adapts to you. Very game-like mechanics translated into narrative. The arena fights are detailed and tactical.
- **Caveat:** Only 2 books out, but they're massive (Iron Prince is 33 hours on Audible). Ongoing.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Luke Daniels. Books 1-2 available.

**12. Morcster Chef (Cleaver's Edge #1)** — Actus
- **Series:** 3 books, complete trilogy
- **Magic System:** Fantasy world with cooking as a progression path. Arek is an orc chef who uses:
  - Cooking skills that provide buffs and bonuses
  - Knowledge of ingredients and their magical properties
  - Crafting/preparation as a form of magic
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Cooking-focused, but interacts with the wider magic system of the adventuring party.
- **Progression:** Yes — developing recipes, learning ingredient properties, becoming a better chef.
- **Tone:** Light, humorous, found family with adventurer party.
- **Why for you:** Crafting as the central mechanic, but cooking-flavored. Unique angle on "support class" progression.
- **Caveat:** Described as "LitRPG lite" — it has some game-like elements (skills, levels mentioned) but they're backgrounded compared to typical LitRPG. The cooking and character interactions are the focus, not stat screens. Worth checking a sample to see if it crosses your tolerance threshold.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Peter Berkrot. Complete trilogy bundle available.

---

- Shades of Magic (magic as resource varying by world)

**For superhero with power oversight:**
- Grimnoir Chronicles (1930s secret societies, government registration)
- Vicious (dark, focused duology)
- Corpies (corporate heroes, different tier of powered people)

Here's what I found about Brian McClellan's Powder Mage trilogy:

## The Trilogy

The Powder Mage trilogy is a series of epic fantasy novels written by American author Brian McClellan. It consists of the novels Promise of Blood (2013), The Crimson Campaign (2014) and The Autumn Republic (2015).(no content)In 2014, Promise of Blood received the Morningstar Award for Best Fantasy Newcomer.

## Audiobooks

The audiobook series is written by Brian McClellan and narrated by Christian Rodska.(no content)Christian Rodska does an outstanding job narrating this trilogy. The audiobooks are available on platforms like Audible and Everand.

## The Magic System

The trilogy features multiple forms of magic:

1. **Powder Mages**: Powder Mages are wizards with the ability to metabolize gunpowder and use it as fuel for various magical powers, including telekinesis; they can also manipulate gunpowder, such as causing it to explode spontaneously. Tamas and Taniel are both powder mages.

2. **Privileged**: Privileged are powerful sorcerers; being exceedingly rare, they are almost exclusively gathered into "Royal Cabals" in direct service to the Nine Kingdoms' various monarchs.

3. **Knacks**: The third form is a Knack that people can have, this Knacks can vastly vary from not needing sleep, to having perfect memory, to being able to know when people tell lies.

4. **Bone-Eye Magic**: The fourth is a slight mystery, and it's a magic employed by "savages" and seems to closely resemble Voodoo (Real Voodoo Dolls among other magics).

## Setting &amp; Expanded Universe

The trilogy primarily takes place in the fictional kingdom of Adro, one of the Nine Kingdoms founded by Kresimir, a semi-mythical figure now worshiped as a deity. At the beginning of Promise of Blood, Field Marshal Tamas has just committed a coup d'etat against Adro's corrupt and ineffective monarchy.(no content)Several short stories and novellas set in the world of The Powder Mage trilogy have been published, as well as an additional trilogy called Gods of Blood and Powder.(no content)The way McClellan's creative vision strikes a balance between classic fantasy magic and the novel addition of gunpowder-based abilities is impressive.

## Popular Recommendations

### Mistborn Trilogy by Brandon Sanderson
The Mistborn trilogy gives us one of the best female characters seen in a fantasy audiobook series.(no content)Together with a criminal who discovers his magical powers, they must fight against the Dark Lord, who rules the land where ash falls from the sky as mist dominates the night. The magic system in this trilogy is called "Allomancy" and captivates every listener.(no content)Michael Kramer narrates this book with his sardonic and humorous style.

### The Kingkiller Chronicle by Patrick Rothfuss
This fantasy trilogy tells the life story of an adventurer and famous musician, Kvothe, who grows to become the most notorious wizard his world has ever seen. Presented like an autobiography, Kvothe narrates his tale to a scribe. The saga happens in a fictional world called Temerant, which has a unique system of magic that combines alchemy and medieval engineering. (Note: This series is not yet complete)

### The Fae &amp; Alchemy Series by Callie Hart
The first of her kind to tread the frozen mountains of Yvelia in over a thousand years, Saeris mistakenly binds herself to Kingfisher, a handsome Fae warrior. He will use her Alchemist's magic to protect his people, no matter what it costs.(no content)From USA Today bestselling author Callie Hart comes a brand new, highly addicting enemies-to-lovers romantasy.(no content)Narrated in duet style.

### Master of the Five Magics by Lyndon Hardy
Lyndon Hardy wrote this book where the first of the disciplines studied by the main protagonist was alchemy. There was a sequel called Secret of the Sixth Magic.

### Other Notable Alchemy-Themed Fantasy Books:
- The Green Lion Trilogy by Teresa Edgerton includes Child of Saturn, The Moon in Hiding, and The Work of the Sun. The setting is medieval and Celtic, with alchemical symbolism and references woven throughout.
- In an alchemy-tinged Rumpelstiltskin retelling, Sepha is an exceptional teen alchemist who can't transmute straw into gold, leaving her in a tricky situation when imprisoned. To save her life, she makes a deal with a conniving magician.

## Top Recommendations

### Brandon Sanderson's Works
The primary type of magic used in the Mistborn books is Allomancy, wherein a genetically gifted user can swallow and "burn" a specific type of metal to temporarily gain a specific supernatural ability.(no content)There are 16 different types of metal Allomancers can use, each of which grants a certain power. Most Allomancers can only burn one kind of metal and are known as "Mistings." However, the rare "Mistborn" can burn all types of metals, making them some of the most powerful characters.(no content)Brandon Sanderson is a fantasy titan exalted by Redditors for his airtight systems of magic. As one Reddit user raves about Mistborn, "the magic is at once mysterious and yet with clearly defined rules that it adheres to strictly."

### Completed Series to Consider

**The Riyria Revelations** by Michael J. Sullivan starts off with a typical rogue-ish cast and classic fantasy tropes, but quickly turns into one of the best fantasy series of all time. These books are easy to read with characters you will absolutely fall in love with.(no content)**Malazan Book of the Fallen** by Steven Erikson is described as the most difficult fantasy series in the world, but absolutely worth the time and effort. It's recommended for those looking for a challenging completed fantasy series.(no content)**Codex Alera** by Jim Butcher is described as "Pokemon meets ancient Rome." This premise is brought to life through amazing characters and intense plotting that will propel you through the six books in the series.(no content)**Age of the Five** offers a fascinating look into religion, colonisation, and an awesome magic system, making it a perfect fantasy series to start.

### Other Notable Mentions

Reddit also recommends **Jade City** by Fonda Lee (wuxia martial arts with Godfather-style crime family saga), **The Jasmine Throne** by Tasha Suri (South Asian fantasy with political intrigue and sapphic romance), and **A Master of Djinn** by P. Djèlí Clark (steampunk fantasy set in 1915 Cairo).(no content)**The Magicians** trilogy by Lev Grossman features a unique magic system where no wands are used. Instead, the characters use an intricate series of hand and finger movements to perform magic.(no content)According to Goodreads' community voting (2,646 books, 8,767 votes), the top books for most interesting magic systems include Mistborn by Brandon Sanderson and The Name of the Wind by Patrick Rothfuss.

Based on the search results, here's what I found about **Gods of Blood and Powder** by Brian McClellan:

## Overview
Gods of Blood and Powder is the second trilogy of books set in Brian McClellan's Powder Mage universe. Its story picks up just over ten years after the events of the original Powder Mage Trilogy, and focuses on the western continent of Fatrasta.

## The Books in the Trilogy
The complete trilogy includes:
- **The Mad Lancers** (Gods of Blood and Powder, #0.1) - a prequel novella published in 2017
- **Sins of Empire** (Book 1)
- **Wrath of Empire** (Book 2)
- **Blood of Empire** (Book 3)

## Story Setting
A new epic fantasy trilogy about a young nation at odds with the ancient forces that have begun to stir as fortune seekers and sorcerers flock to the frontier, set in Brian McClellan's Powder Mage trilogy world. The young nation of Fatrasta is a turbulent place—a frontier destination for criminals, fortune-hunters, brave settlers, and sorcerers seeking relics of the past. Only the iron will of the lady chancellor and her secret police holds the capital city of Landfall together.

## Main Characters
The insurrection that threatens Landfall must be purged with guile and force, a task which falls on the shoulders of a spy named Michel Bravis, convicted war hero Mad Ben Styke, and Lady Vlora Flint, a mercenary general with a past as turbulent as Landfall's present.

## Development History
In February 2015, The Autumn Republic concluded the planned Powder Mage trilogy. McClellan then published a sequel trilogy that had tentatively been entitled "Goddess of the Empire" before being replaced by the more thematically over-arching "Gods of Blood and Powder."(no content)All three books in the Gods of Blood and Powder Trilogy are available, including as a signed bundle in trade paperback format from the author's website.

Here's what I found about Robert Jackson Bennett's **Divine Cities Trilogy**:

## The Trilogy

The series consists of City of Stairs (The Divine Cities, #1), City of Blades (The Divine Cities, #2), City of Miracles (The Divine Cities, #3), and The Divine Cities Trilogy (omnibus edition).(no content)A special omnibus edition collects all three books of Robert Jackson Bennett's acclaimed Divine Cities trilogy in a single volume.

## Audiobook Availability

The audiobook of City of Stairs is produced by Recorded Books (©2014 Robert Jackson Bennett, ℗2014 Recorded Books).(no content)Amazon offers Whispersync for Voice, allowing you to switch between reading the Kindle book and listening to the Audible audiobook, with reduced pricing available when you buy the Kindle book first.

## The Magic System / World

In a world where terrifying, capricious gods once walked the earth, enslaving and brutalizing millions, three unforgettable protagonists struggle to come to terms with the mysteries these divinities left behind—and to make sure these cruel masters do not rise again.(no content)The city of Bulikov once wielded the powers of the gods to conquer the world, enslaving and brutalizing millions—until its divine protectors were killed. Now Bulikov has become just another colonial outpost, but the surreal landscape of the city itself—first shaped, now shattered, by the thousands of miracles its guardians once worked upon it—stands as a constant, haunting reminder of its former supremacy.(no content)World building was well blended with a brisk story line. Readers are immersed in a world where the time of divinities is past and the world must deal with the lingering presence of their worshippers and their persistent miracles.(no content)The series explores the transition from a society of magic (essentially) to one of technology.(no content)Readers have noted that they "loved the way the magic system works in these books."

## Critical Acclaim

City of Stairs was shortlisted for the Locus Award and the World Fantasy Award. City of Blades was a finalist for the 2015 World Fantasy, Locus, and British Fantasy Awards. The entire Divine Cities trilogy was nominated for a Hugo Award for Best Series.(no content)NPR described it as "A great world, original and unique, with a scent and a texture, a sense of deep, bloody history, and a naturally blended magic living in the stones."

Here's what I found about the Riyria Revelations series by Michael J. Sullivan:

## Series Overview

The Riyria Revelations is a series of high fantasy novels written by Michael J. Sullivan and published by Orbit Books in 2011 and 2012. The series consists of three original titles: Theft of Swords, Rise of Empire, and Heir of Novron.(no content)The books were previously self-published as a six-volume series selling 90,000 copies.

## Complete Book List

The series was published in two different ways—six books originally self-published and three two-book omnibus editions. The original versions are out of print, having been replaced by Orbit releases.

The original six books are:
1. The Crown Conspiracy (2008), 2. Avempartha (2009), 3. Nyphron Rising (2009), 4. The Emerald Storm (2010), 5. Wintertide (2010), 6. Percepliquis (2011)

## Magic System

One reviewer notes: "If you wanted a complex magic system with all the bells and whistles as Brandon or Jordan does, this may not be for you." The series features magic but doesn't focus heavily on elaborate, systematic magic rules.

Characters like Arista use "magic taught to her by Esrahaddon", and the wizard Esrahaddon plays a significant role, with Royce suspecting him of "using the thieves as pawns in his own game."

## Audiobooks

GraphicAudio has, since 2008, produced full-cast dramatised audio adaptations of Sullivan's entire Riyria bibliography.(no content)Volume 3 of the Riyria Revelations contains the final two books of the series, book #5 Wintertide and book #6 Percepliquis. Michael J. Sullivan and Tim Gerard Reynolds reunite to bring all of the main characters back. The audiobook is narrated by Tim Gerard Reynolds.(no content)Regarding audiobook lengths: Book 1 (Theft of Swords) is 22 hours, Book 2 (Rise of Empire) is 26 hours, and Book 3 (Heir of Novron) is 31 hours.

## Related Series

Sullivan has written a series of novels entitled The Riyria Chronicles that take place before the events in Riyria Revelations, following the early adventures of Royce Melborn and Hadrian Blackwater. The first two novels, The Crown Tower and The Rose and the Thorn, were released in August and September 2013.(no content)The Riyria Revelations series (2011-2012) was published before The Riyria Chronicles (2013-present) but is set after it chronologically. Sullivan has recommended reading the two series in publication order.

## The Complete Trilogy

The trilogy consists of three books: Book 1: Priestess of the White, Book 2: Last of the Wilds, and Book 3: Voice of the Gods.(no content)It's a trilogy of fantasy novels recounting the story of Auraya, a young priestess who rises to the highest rank in her world's religious hierarchy, only to find that there may be more to the gods she worships than she was led to believe.(no content)All three volumes of the Age of the Five trilogy were Sunday Times bestsellers.

## Magic System &amp; Plot Elements

In a magical land beset by hidden enemies, the gods call upon five extraordinary humans to unite their peoples in peace. Courageous young Auraya never imagined she would be chosen, but as the newest Priestess of the White, endowed with phenomenal powers, she has little time to adjust before facing a perilous challenge.(no content)An enduring friendship with a Dreamweaver—a member of an ancient outcast sect of sorcerer-healers—could threaten Auraya's future.(no content)The White are the avatars of the Five Gods. The priestess Auraya is sent on an urgent mission to reconcile with the powerful, outcast Dreamweavers, for their magical healing abilities may be the key to saving the land.

## Audiobook Availability

## About the Author

Trudi Canavan published her first story in 1999 and it received an Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story. She lives with her partner in Melbourne, Australia, and spends her time writing, painting and weaving.

Here's what I found about Lyndon Hardy's "Master of the Five Magics" series:

## About the Series

*Master of the Five Magics* is a fantasy novel by Lyndon Hardy, first published in 1980. It is the first of a trilogy set in the same world; the second book is *Secret of the Sixth Magic* and the third *Riddle of the Seven Realms*.(no content)Hardy is a New York Times best-selling author of the "Magic by the Numbers" fantasy series. *One Last Heist*, the seventh book in the series, is now available.

## The Magic System

A primary focus of the plot is upon the five magics of the title: Thaumaturgy, Alchemy, Magic, Sorcery, and Wizardry. In the system devised for the trilogy, each discipline allows the user to perform magical actions within a particular set of rules.(no content)The author melds physics with the fantasy of alchemy, sorcery, and wizardry to produce tales in which there are constraints and limitations. Magic is not omnipotent. When the protagonists are in a jam, they are not saved with a simple "bibbity, bobbiity, boo."

## Series Structure

With the exception that book 5, *Magic Times Three*, involves the same protagonists as book 4, *The Archimage's Fourth Daughter*, all the books in the series have different leading characters. They can be read in any order.

## The Story

Alodar, the mere journeyman, learning the least of the five crafts of magic. He had no right to aspire for the queen's hand—but aspire he did! Alodar's quest takes him from one magical craft to another—each with its own distinct powers and pitfalls.

## Cultural Impact

It was a popular enough book that it influenced a song by Megadeth called "Five Magics." The five color magic code in the "Magic: The Gathering" card games was also inspired by "Master of the Five Magics."

## Audiobook Availability

One source mentions a "Master Of The Five Magics Audiobook" available with Audible MP3 Download by Lyndon Hardy. However, the search results don't provide extensive details about audiobook versions for the complete series. You may want to check Audible or other audiobook platforms directly for the full series availability.

## The Complete Series

The Faithful and the Fallen is a 4-book collection by John Gwynne. The books in order are:

1. **Malice** - Published by Pan Macmillan in 2012, it won the David Gemmell Morningstar Award for Best Fantasy Debut of 2012.
2. **Valour** (Book 2)
3. **Ruin** (Book 3) - Shortlisted for the 2016 David Gemmell Legend Award for Best Novel.
4. **Wrath** (Book 4)

The following three books in the series – Valour, Ruin and Wrath, were all shortlisted for the David Gemmell Legend Award for Best Fantasy Novels of 2014, 2015 and 2016.

## Audiobooks

## World &amp; Magic System

The series is a tale of blind greed, ambition, and betrayal set in a world where ancient monsters are reawakening -- and a war to end all wars is about to begin.(no content)The main story is about the coming of a God-War which essentially encompasses the good side who are the followers of Elyon and the bad side who are the followers of Asroth who was imprisoned.

Key elements include:
- Classic fantasy ingredients: a chosen one, a grizzled mentor, a bond between boy and beast (a wolf), giants, magic artifacts, prophecies, and the looming sense that an ancient evil is stirring once more.
- The Seven Treasures play a significant role, with the cauldron being described as the most powerful of these treasures.
- The Banished Lands has a violent past where armies of men and giants clashed in battle. Although the giant-clans were broken in ages past, giants now stir anew, the very stones weep blood and there are sightings of giant wyrms.
- Sorrow will darken the world, as angels and demons make it their battlefield. Then there will be a war to end all wars.

## Of Blood and Bone Trilogy

The series is set in the same world as The Faithful and the Fallen series.(no content)It's a direct sequel series set 100+ years after The Faithful and the Fallen, exploring a fragile peace unraveling into new conflicts.

### The Complete Trilogy:
The three books are:
- **A Time of Dread** (2018) – Book 1
- **A Time of Blood** (2019) – Book 2
- **A Time of Courage** (2020) – Book 3

### Connection to The Faithful and the Fallen

The Of Blood and Bone series takes place in the same world as The Faithful and the Fallen, but about 130 years later.(no content)The two series are related, and the events of the first series have become the history of the second series, but all that you need to know is in A Time of Dread, book one Of Blood and Bone.(no content)You do not need to have read the first series in order to read this series. The books are long, but deservedly so. You'd get more from all the small mentions and history and lore if you read the previous series first.

### The Faithful and the Fallen (4 books):
- Malice (2012)
- Valor (2014)
- Ruin (2015)(no content)- Wrath (2016)

### Recommended Reading Order
For the chronological Banished Lands order (recommended for immersion): The Faithful and the Fallen (Books 1-4) → Of Blood and Bone (Books 5-7).

Here's what I found about the Black Magician Trilogy by Trudi Canavan:

## The Black Magician Trilogy

Trudi Canavan is the author of the bestselling Black Magician trilogy—The Magician's Guild, The Novice, and The High Lord.(no content)She published her first story in 1999 and received an Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story. Her debut series, the Black Magician trilogy, made her an international success.

### The Story &amp; Magic System

Each year the magicians of Imardin gather together to purge the city streets of vagrants, urchins and miscreants. Masters of the disciplines of magic, they know that no one can oppose them.(no content)But their protective shield is not as impenetrable as they believe. Sonea, angry, frustrated and outraged by the treatment of her family and friends, hurls a stone at the shield, putting all her rage behind it. To the amazement of all who bear witness, the stone passes unhindered through the barrier and renders a magician unconscious.(no content)What the Magicians' Guild has long dreaded has finally come to pass. There is someone outside their ranks who possesses a raw power beyond imagining, an untrained mage who must be found and schooled before she destroys herself and her city with a force she cannot yet control.

### The Guild &amp; Black Magic

The Traitor Spy Trilogy takes place a generation after the events of the Black Magician Trilogy. Black magic is no longer forbidden to Guild magicians, but the knowledge and practice of it is severely restricted.(no content)In accepting the protection of the guild's high lord, Sonea may have embraced an even bleaker fate. For High Lord Akkarin harbours a secret that is far darker than his magician's robes.

### Audiobook Editions

An unabridged audio edition was published by Bolinda Audio Books, and an abridged audio edition was published by Time Warner AudioBooks UK.(no content)The audiobook of Book 1 is narrated by Richard Aspel and published by Bolinda Publishing Pty Ltd. The listening length is 15 hours and 23 minutes.(no content)Book 2, The Novice, is also narrated by Richard Aspel with a listening length of 18 hours and 34 minutes.

The audiobooks are available on multiple platforms including Audible and Apple Books, with Book 1 priced at $4.99.

## Series Status

**Arcane Ascension 6 came out this year, and Arcane Ascension 5 in audio as well**, so it's been a big year for book releases.(no content)Reception for both Arcane Ascension 5 and 6 has generally been excellent. There have been some complaints — some people didn't like the political focus of book 5, for example, or the interludes in book 6 — but overall, they've been better received than Books 3 and 4 were.

## Completion Status

The series is **not yet complete**. Book 7 is planned as "the last book in the main Arcane Ascension series."(no content)Andrew Rowe expects most of next year to be taken up by work on Arcane Ascension 7. After working on Weapons &amp; Wielders 4, Arcane Ascension 7 is currently next on his list, and he hopes to finish and release it next year.

- **Books 1-6**: Published
- **Book 7**: In progress (expected to be the final book in the main series)
- **Series complete?**: No, one more book to go

Here are the search results for the Ranger's Apprentice audiobook series by John Flanagan:

## Series Overview

Ranger's Apprentice is a series written by Australian author John Flanagan. It began as twenty short stories Flanagan wrote for his son to get him interested in reading. Ten years later, Flanagan found the stories again and decided to turn them into a book, which became the first novel in the series, The Ruins of Gorlan.(no content)The series follows the adventures of Will, an orphan, who is chosen as an apprentice Ranger, one of the skilled trackers, archers, and warriors in the service of the King of Araluen. Will strives to keep the Kingdom of Araluen safe from invaders, traitors, and other threats. He is joined on his adventures by his mentor, Halt, and his best friend Horace.

## Complete Audiobook Collection

The Ranger's Apprentice Complete Audiobook Series by John Flanagan includes 1197 files across tales like "The Ruins of Gorlan" and "The Emperor of Nihon-Ja" in a 4.14 GiB collection.(no content)The main series consists of 11 books (Ranger's Apprentice 1-11) by John Flanagan.

## Audiobook Availability

- **Amazon/Audible**: The Ruins of Gorlan audiobook is available on Audible, narrated by William Zappa and published by Bolinda Publishing Pty Ltd.

- **OverDrive (Library access)**: Ranger's Apprentice has 78 entries in the series available through OverDrive.

- **AudiobookStore**: "The Lost Stories" audiobook is read by John Keating, published by Listening Library, with a listen time of 13 hours at 1.0x speed.

## Related Series

There is also a prequel series called "The Early Years," a sequel/spin-off series called "Brotherband Chronicles," and another sequel/spin-off called "Ranger's Apprentice: The Royal Ranger."

Based on my search, here's what I found about Travis Baldree's Legends &amp; Lattes series:

## The Series So Far

**Bookshops &amp; Bonedust** is a fantasy novel written by American author Travis Baldree. It was first published in trade paperback and ebook by Tor Books and in audiobook by Macmillan Audio in November, 2023. It is a prequel to the author's 2022 novel Legends &amp; Lattes.(no content)Although written after Legends and Lattes, it chronologically takes place two decades before it.

## Book Details

Bookshops &amp; Bonedust became an Instant #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Indie Bestseller, and was named a Barnes &amp; Noble Best Fantasy Book of 2023 and an Amazon Best Science Fiction and Fantasy Book of 2023.(no content)The story follows Viv, an orc mercenary who is contracted to fight the necromancer Varine the Pale. Her leg is injured in her very first fight, and her boss leaves her in the town of Murk to recover. In Murk, Viv befriends a bookseller named Fern and meets the gnome Gallina, beginning a summer romance with a dwarf baker named Maylee.

## Author's Notes on the Prequel

The author did not plan to write this prequel. As Baldree wrote: "So here we are, with a prequel I never intended to write. And I'm happy with it. It says things I want to say, and if I'm lucky, it interlocks with Legends &amp; Lattes in a way that makes both stories better, while still allowing them to stand on their own."

## Future Books

Baldree has mentioned three more standalone fantasy novels in this series will be written and published, and the first one is slated to be released in 2025.

## Current Reading Order

1. **Legends &amp; Lattes** (2022) - The original novel
2. **Bookshops &amp; Bonedust** (2023) - The prequel (listed as #0 on Goodreads)

The series is known for popularizing the "cozy fantasy" subgenre, featuring low-stakes, heartwarming stories set in high-fantasy worlds.

Le Guin, Paperback | Barnes &amp; Noble®","url":"https://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/a-wizard-of-earthsea-ursula-k-le-guin/1100818986"}]

Based on the search results, here's information about Ursula K. Le Guin's Earthsea series, its magic system, and audiobooks:

## The Earthsea Series

*A Wizard of Earthsea*, first published in 1968, is a seminal fantasy novel by Ursula K. Le Guin. Set in the fictional archipelago of Earthsea, it follows the coming-of-age journey of a young mage named Ged as he struggles to master his powers and confront a shadowy evil he has unleashed.(no content)Le Guin produced The Earthsea Cycle between 1968 and 2001. She had not planned to start a series for young adults, but began working on *A Wizard of Earthsea* at the request of her publisher.(no content)The series is described as a tetralogy that includes *The Tombs of Atuan* and *The Farthest Shore*, introducing the listener to Ged, the greatest sorcerer in all Earthsea, known also as Sparrowhawk.

## The True Names Magic System

The novel established many elements that would define the series, including its Taoist-influenced magic system based on true names and cosmic equilibrium.(no content)The magic system is based on knowing the true names of things, giving wizards power over them.(no content)Le Guin produces among the most interesting magic systems ever made, all based upon the true names of things. A wizard who knows a thing's true name has power over it.(no content)At the age of 13, the boy receives his true name - Ged - and gives himself over to the gentle tutelage of the Master Ogion.

## Audiobook Availability

The Earthsea Cycle is narrated by several esteemed voice actors, including actor Rob Inglis (who also lends his voice to the Lord of the Rings audiobooks), critically acclaimed British actress Jenny Sterlin, and English television and film star Samuel Roukin.(no content)Audiobook readings have been made by different narrators and publishers.(no content)There is also *The Complete Earthsea Series &amp; The Left Hand of Darkness* available on Audible.

## Awards and Legacy

Books in The Earthsea Cycle have won numerous awards, including the World Fantasy Award for Best Novel, a Nebula Award for Best Novel, a National Book Award, and a Newbery Honor.(no content)*The Books of Earthsea* (complete illustrated edition) was published in 2018 by Saga Press and won the 2019 Hugo Award for Best Art Book and the 2019 Locus Award for Best Art Book.

Here's what I found about **The Deed of Paksenarrion** by Elizabeth Moon:

## Overview

The Deed of Paksenarrion is available complete in a single hardcover volume and has been described as "the Finest Trilogy of Epic Fantasy in a Decade." Paksenarrion, a simple sheepfarmer's daughter, yearns for a life of adventure and glory.

## The Trilogy Structure

The complete trilogy consists of three books:
- Paks' journey through **Sheepfarmer's Daughter**, **Divided Allegiance** and **Oath of Gold**(no content)**Book One:** Paks is trained as a mercenary, blooded, and introduced to the life of a soldier and to the followers of Gird, the soldier's god. **Book Two:** Paks leaves the Duke's company to follow the path of Gird alone—and on her lonely quests encounters the other sentient races of her world. **Book Three:** Paks the warrior must learn to live with Paks the human. She undertakes a holy quest for a lost elven prince that brings the gods' wrath down on her and tests her very limits.

## Paladins and Magic

It will surprise no one familiar with this trilogy to learn that their primary inspiration was the Dungeons &amp; Dragons paladin character class. Paladins are the knight in shining armor type characters, who derive their power as warriors and magic-users from their pure and noble virtues.(no content)The series is considered "a very unique and enjoyable low-fantasy epic, and probably my favourite portrayal of paladins in fiction."

## Audiobook Availability

The Deed of Paksenarrion audiobooks are available on Audible. Free trial available!(no content)The audiobook was produced in 2010 by Audible, Inc., with the original copyright from 1988 belonging to Elizabeth Moon.(no content)Oath of Gold (Book 3) audiobook is narrated by Jennifer Van Dyck and produced by Audible Studios.

## Awards and Author Background

The first novel of the Deed of Paksenarrion series went on to win the Compton Crook Award in the category of Best First Fantasy Novel, which was awarded by the Baltimore Fiction Society.(no content)Elizabeth Moon has degrees in history and biology, served as a commissioned officer in the U.S. Marine Corps, was elected to public office, and spent six years as a paramedic on a rural Texas ambulance service. Her much acclaimed novels include The Deed of Paksenarrion, an epic fantasy, and the "Heris Serrano" series.

Here's what I found about the Wheel of Time magic system:

## The One Power

Every character who uses the One Power in Robert Jordan's Wheel of Time books draws it from the same place: the True Source. Described in the novels as the "driving force of the universe," the One Power's True Source is infinite and can never be depleted.(no content)The One Power (the in-universe name for magic) spins the celestial Wheel of Time, which weaves the Great Pattern, enfolding the world, all life and time itself.

## Saidin and Saidar

The True Source is divided into two halves: saidar and saidin.(no content)Once, both men and women could become powerful Aes Sedai, but they connected to different sides of the One Power. Women connect to saidar, while only men use saidin.(no content)Saidar is described as a gentle, but infinitely powerful river; a force which will do what you wish it to, but requires patience to be "persuaded." A woman must submit to saidar in order to access it, an act universally known as embracing the Power.(no content)Using saidin is more of a struggle than it is for saidar.(no content)During the Breaking of the World, the Dark One touched saidin, corrupting the male half of the One Power. As a result, any man who channels is doomed to madness.

## The Five Powers and Weaves

When using the One Power one weaves flows of different elements: Earth, Spirit, Water, Air, and Fire, also known as the Five Powers.(no content)Men are generally stronger with Fire and Earth, while women are generally stronger with Air and Water; significant strength in Spirit is distributed equally, and relatively rare in either.(no content)Weaves of the One Power are similar to textile weaves, and weaving Saidar has been compared to folding silk. Once a weave has been created, the channeler can "hold" it to keep the effect ongoing, or knot the flows, a process called "tying the weave off". A weave that has been tied off persists even after the channeler has released the True Source.(no content)A channeler of Saidin or Saidar is able to see the weaves created using the same half of the Power, but not the other. For this reason, a man cannot teach a woman how to create a weave and vice versa.

## Examples of Weaves

There are many different things that can be accomplished using the One Power. For example, channelers can heal injuries and sickness, find ores or metals in the ground, throw fireballs from their hands, call lightning from the sky, control the weather and winds, travel instantaneously from one place to another, change their appearance, and even control someone else's actions through Compulsion.(no content)Some abilities are a bit more complicated and necessitate the use of three threads, with one example of this being Healing. To heal someone, one must weave flows of Air, Water, and Spirit.

## Linking

Women are more dexterous in the actual weaving of the flows, and have the advantage of linking, but cannot increase a circle beyond thirteen without the inclusion of men. When a male channeler and a female channeler work together they are much stronger than many of the same gender, it is said that this is caused by saidin and saidar resonating.

Note: The search results didn't return specific information about Wheel of Time audiobooks. If you're looking for audiobook information specifically, I can search for that separately.

I have comprehensive research. Here's my final set of 12 recommendations:

---

## Final 12 Recommendations: Complete Series with Interesting Magic

---

### CATEGORIZED/SYSTEMATIC MAGIC

**1. Promise of Blood (Powder Mage #1)** — Brian McClellan
- **Series:** 3 books complete. Sequel trilogy (Gods of Blood and Powder) also complete — 6 books total in the universe.
- **Magic System:** Three distinct types, clearly categorized:
  - *Powder Mages:* Ingest gunpowder to enhance senses, guide bullets, ignite powder at distance. Snorting a line of gunpowder gives a "powder trance" of heightened abilities.
  - *Privileged:* Traditional elemental sorcerers wearing gloves with runes. Powerful but vulnerable without their gloves.
  - *Knacks:* Minor magical talents — perfect memory, lie detection, not needing sleep, etc.
- **Build Variety:** HIGH. Each magic type plays differently. Powder Mages are tactical snipers, Privileged are artillery, Knacks provide utility.
- **Tone:** Military fantasy, flintlock era. Coup d'état opens the series.
- **Why for you:** Explicit categorization of magic types. The interplay between them (Powder Mages were created specifically to counter Privileged) is very game-design-y.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Christian Rodska. Complete series available.

**2. Master of the Five Magics** — Lyndon Hardy
- **Series:** 3 books complete (Master of the Five Magics, Secret of the Sixth Magic, Riddle of the Seven Realms)
- **Magic System:** Five completely distinct magical disciplines, each with different rules:
  - *Thaumaturgy:* Sympathetic magic — like affects like, once together always together
  - *Alchemy:* Transformation through precise formulas and procedures
  - *Magic:* Crafting objects of power through ritual
  - *Sorcery:* Illusion and mind control through eye contact
  - *Wizardry:* Summoning and binding demons for knowledge/power
- **Build Variety:** EXTREMELY HIGH. The protagonist learns each discipline sequentially, and they don't overlap — completely different skillsets.
- **Tone:** Classic fantasy adventure. The hero is a journeyman who must master multiple crafts.
- **Why for you:** This book influenced Magic: The Gathering's five-color system. Each magic has explicit rules and limitations. Very systematic.
- **Audible:** Available. Older series but still in print.

**3. A Wizard of Earthsea (Earthsea Cycle #1)** — Ursula K. Le Guin
- **Series:** 5 novels + short stories, complete
- **Magic System:** True Names magic — knowing something's true name gives you power over it:
  - Everything has a true name in the Old Speech
  - Wizards spend years learning names of things
  - Speaking a name allows control, but everything has consequences
  - The world operates on balance — every action creates reaction
- **Build Variety:** LOW in traditional sense. All wizards use the same system, but mastery varies enormously.
- **Progression:** YES. Ged starts as an arrogant student and becomes the greatest mage alive through hard lessons.
- **Tone:** Contemplative, mythic, Taoist-influenced. Not action-heavy.
- **Why for you:** The "true names" concept influenced countless later works (including much of fantasy gaming). Foundational text for systematic magic.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Rob Inglis (Lord of the Rings narrator). Complete cycle available.

---

### DIVINE/RELIGIOUS MAGIC

**4. City of Stairs (Divine Cities #1)** — Robert Jackson Bennett
- **Series:** 3 books, complete (City of Stairs, City of Blades, City of Miracles)
- **Magic System:** Dead gods left miracles behind that still work:
  - Six Divinities once ruled, each with different domains and miracles
  - When the gods were killed, their miracles became unstable — doors that lead nowhere, buildings with impossible geometry, blessed items with lingering power
  - Investigating what the miracles do and why they persist is central to the plot
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Different gods left different miracle-types. Understanding which god created what matters.
- **Tone:** Spy thriller meets fantasy. Post-colonial themes — the former slaves now rule the former masters.
- **Why for you:** Same author as Foundryside (which you liked). Similar "magic as a system to be understood" approach, but with divine rather than technological framing.
- **Audible:** Complete trilogy available.

**5. Priestess of the White (Age of the Five #1)** — Trudi Canavan
- **Series:** 3 books, complete
- **Magic System:** Five gods grant powers to their chosen priests (the White):
  - Each god has a domain and grants related abilities
  - Priests can also learn general magic (healing, combat)
  - Dreamweavers are an outcast sect with different magic — they enter dreams to heal minds
  - Conflict between religious magical traditions drives the plot
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Different gods, different specializations.
- **Progression:** YES. Auraya rises from novice to one of the most powerful White.
- **Tone:** Religious intrigue, war, questioning faith.
- **Why for you:** Explores how magical power interacts with religious institutions. The Dreamweavers represent an alternative tradition.
- **Audible:** Complete trilogy available.

---

### GUILD/TRAINING MAGIC

**6. The Magicians' Guild (Black Magician Trilogy #1)** — Trudi Canavan
- **Series:** 3 books complete (+ sequel trilogy also complete if you want more)
- **Magic System:** Guild-controlled magic in a society where magic is known and regulated:
  - Magicians draw from personal magical reserves
  - Different disciplines: Healing, Warrior, Alchemy
  - "Black magic" (drawing power from others) is forbidden — but the High Lord has a secret
  - Magic must be trained or it eventually kills the untrained wielder
- **Build Variety:** MEDIUM. Different disciplines exist, though the protagonist's path is somewhat fixed.
- **Progression:** YES. Sonea goes from slum girl with uncontrolled power to trained magician navigating politics.
- **Tone:** Academy politics, class conflict, dark secrets.
- **Not hidden world:** Magic is publicly known. The Guild controls who can practice.
- **Why for you:** Training progression, magic as institutional power, clear rules about how magic works and why it's dangerous untrained.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Richard Aspel. Complete trilogy available.

**7. Sheepfarmer's Daughter (Deed of Paksenarrion #1)** — Elizabeth Moon
- **Series:** 3 books, complete (omnibus available as "The Deed of Paksenarrion")
- **Magic System:** Paladin powers granted through faith and virtue:
  - Paladins gain abilities (healing, sensing evil, combat prowess) through devotion to their god
  - Power can be lost if faith wavers or virtue fails
  - Different gods grant different flavors of paladin abilities
  - The cost of power is genuine moral commitment
- **Build Variety:** LOW in mechanical sense — but the "paladin progression" is deeply explored.
- **Progression:** YES. Paks goes from farmgirl to mercenary to paladin across three books.
- **Tone:** Military fantasy, then religious quest. Realistic portrayal of soldier life.
- **Why for you:** Best portrayal of paladins in fantasy. If you've ever wanted to understand how "paladin as a class" could work narratively, this is the book.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Jennifer Van Dyck. Complete trilogy available.

---

### EPIC/ARTIFACT FANTASY

**8. Theft of Swords (Riyria Revelations #1)** — Michael J. Sullivan
- **Series:** 3 omnibus volumes (6 original books), complete. Prequel series also complete.
- **Magic System:** Lighter magic presence — wizards exist but are rare:
  - Ancient elven magic underlies the world
  - Artifacts from the old empire have power
  - Magic is mysterious rather than systematic
- **Build Variety:** LOW for magic specifically. The protagonists are a thief and a swordsman, not mages.
- **Progression:** Character growth rather than power progression.
- **Tone:** LIGHT. Fun adventure, witty banter, likeable rogues. "Comfort food fantasy."
- **Why for you:** Palette cleanser. If you want something that's just enjoyable without complex systems. Tim Gerard Reynolds narration is excellent.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Tim Gerard Reynolds. Complete series available.

**9. Malice (Faithful and the Fallen #1)** — John Gwynne
- **Series:** 4 books, complete. Sequel trilogy (Of Blood and Bone) also complete.
- **Magic System:** Ancient artifacts and divine conflict:
  - The Seven Treasures are powerful magical items
  - A prophesied God-War approaches between followers of Elyon and Asroth
  - Giants, wyrms, and other creatures have their own magic
  - Magic is more mythic than systematic
- **Build Variety:** LOW in mechanical sense. Different characters have different roles (warrior, spy, etc.) but not "builds."
- **Progression:** YES. Multiple characters grow from youths to warriors/leaders.
- **Tone:** Epic, violent, good vs. evil with grey areas. David Gemmell vibes.
- **Why for you:** If you want epic scope and satisfying conclusions. Gwynne also wrote Bloodsworn Saga (which you liked from list 2).
- **Audible:** Narrated by Damian Lynch. Complete series available.

---

### SKILLS-BASED PROGRESSION

**10. The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice #1)** — John Flanagan
- **Series:** 11 books, complete. Spin-off series also complete.
- **Magic System:** Minimal magic. Rangers use skills, not spells:
  - Archery, tracking, stealth, knife-fighting
  - Rangers appear almost magical through extreme competence
  - Actual magic exists in the world but Rangers don't use it
- **Build Variety:** LOW. Rangers have a specific skillset. Other characters (warriors, diplomats) have different roles.
- **Progression:** YES. Will goes from rejected orphan to master Ranger across 11 books.
- **Tone:** YA adventure. Light, fast-paced, mentor-student relationships.
- **Why for you:** "Progression through training" rather than magic. Shows how skill mastery can feel like power growth.
- **Audible:** Narrated by William Zappa. Complete series available.

---

### URBAN FANTASY / LIGHTER TONE

**11. The Utterly Uninteresting and Unadventurous Tales of Fred, the Vampire Accountant** — Drew Hayes
- **Series:** 9 books, complete (final audiobook releases January 2026)
- **Magic System:** Urban fantasy paranormal society:
  - Vampires, werewolves, mages, zombies, dragons all exist
  - Different creatures have different abilities and politics
  - Fred is a vampire accountant — timid, socially awkward, but accidentally keeps saving the day
- **Build Variety:** HIGH across the cast. Each paranormal type has different powers.
- **Progression:** Fred grows more confident and capable, though he remains fundamentally Fred.
- **Tone:** HUMOROUS. Cozy urban fantasy. Found family.
- **Why for you:** Light, fun, complete. Different flavor from epic fantasy. Same author as Super Powereds.
- **Audible:** Narrated by Kirby Heyborne. Books 1-8 available now, book 9 audiobook January 2026.

**12. Legends & Lattes** — Travis Baldree
- **Series:** 2 books (Legends & Lattes, Bookshops & Bonedust), each standalone. More planned but each story is complete.
- **Magic System:** High fantasy world, but the story is low-stakes:
  - Magic exists (the protagonist is a retired barbarian adventurer)
  - But the story is about opening a coffee shop, not fighting monsters
  - Gnomish inventions, subtle enchantments for atmosphere
- **Build Variety:** N/A — not really applicable.
- **Progression:** Personal growth rather than power progression.
- **Tone:** COZY. Slice-of-life. Found family. No combat.
- **Why for you:** You liked Beware of Chicken and Morcster Chef. Same energy. Travis Baldree wrote AND narrates (same voice as Cradle).
- **Caveat:** More books planned, so technically "ongoing" — but each book is a complete standalone story.
- **Audible:** Author-narrated. Both books available.

---

**My suggestions for cutting:**

- **Cut 8 (Art of the Adept)** — You already have The Enchanter for "academy wizard who crafts." Art of the Adept is good but covers similar ground.

- **Cut 15 (City of Stairs)** — You already have Foundryside from the same author. Both explore "magic as system to understand," but Foundryside's scriving is more explicitly programming-like, which seemed to appeal to you.

- **Pick ONE of 9 or 13** — Grimnoir (1930s superpowers) and Powder Mage (flintlock magic categories) both offer "categorized magic types in non-medieval setting." Grimnoir has legendary audiobook narration. Powder Mage has sequel trilogy if you want more.

- **Pick ONE of 5 or 12** — Beware of Chicken and Morcster Chef are both cozy/comedy with crafting elements. Beware of Chicken has Travis Baldree (Cradle narrator). Morcster Chef is complete trilogy, shorter commitment.

**If I had to pick 5 for you:**
- 2 (Jade City) — unique
- 5 (Beware of Chicken) — cozy, Travis Baldree
- 9 (Grimnoir) — legendary narration, 1930s powers
- 10 (Circle of Magic) — unique craft-magic

**Total series commitment if you finish all:** ~45 books

**Narration highlights:**
- Hard Magic (Grimnoir) — Bronson Pinchot, legendary performance
- Beware of Chicken — Travis Baldree (Cradle narrator)
- Art of the Adept — Tim Gerard Reynolds
- Super Powereds — very long books (~25 hrs each)

Good variety: color magic, territory magic, superpowers, enchanting, scriving, linguistic reality-altering, five disciplines, cultivation comedy, wizard progression, 1930s powers, craft magic, gunpowder mages.

Use your 12 credits, then cancel. Enjoy.
